On the Silk Industry of Jiangsu and Zhejiang (Continued)

Shen Wenwei

Opinions on the reform of the silk industry can generally be divided into two factions: rapid and gradual. The gradual faction, represented by schools and government agencies, advocates improving silkworm breeds and silk reeling machinery to reduce costs and improve product quality and value to compete with Japan. The rapid faction, led by Mr. Mo Shangqing, advocates controlling trade, production, and raw material prices, and dumping on the international market to secure an outlet for raw silk, and then gradually engaging in technical improvements. In recent years, there has been considerable progress in technical improvements in the silk industry, such as a sharp increase in the number of improved silkworm breeds. In Wuxi, the improvement of the lotus root system in silk reeling has also been quite significant, as well as the rise of autumn silkworm rearing. In Zhejiang, autumn silkworm rearing has also gradually developed in the past two years. This is a fact that cannot be concealed. The reason why the silk industry is still declining is due to extremely complex economic relations. Mr. Mo Shangqing's plan to unify silk mills in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui is based on Mr. Mo's many years of experience in the raw silk trade, informing us of the importance of the raw silk trade. Mr. Mo's plan is divided into four points: (1) Sales (i.e., trade): using the method of controlling trade to prevent Japanese manipulation of the market and increase the power of trade competition. (2) Implementation: controlling the price of raw materials (cocoons) to avoid blind competition. (3) Production: paying special attention to the allocation of raw materials and labor, unifying the quality of raw silk to meet the needs of large-scale silk mills, increasing efficiency, saving raw materials, and reducing costs. (4) Finance (i.e., financial plan): the plan requires the central government to issue 5 million yuan in public bonds to be distributed to various silk mills, and silk reelers to invest 2.5 million yuan, totaling 7.5 million yuan. This amount is to be used as a advance payment, and interest-bearing loans of 30 million yuan are borrowed from the silver industry, totaling 37.5 million yuan. This amount is used to purchase cocoons produced in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui. Mr. Mo's plan does make up for the lack of technology, but it is doubtful whether the financial resources are sufficient to compete with Japan.

The author wrote [China's Silk Industry and Socialized Management] in 1927 (the copyright of this manuscript was sold to the Shanghai New Learning Society in 1928, but it was burned down in a fire, and then revised in 1931, but it has not been published due to the recession in the book industry at that time). He suggested the systematization of the operation of China's silk industry. In 1928, he also wrote [Opinions on the Development of the Zhejiang Silk Industry], which he submitted to Mr. Cheng Zhenjun, the director of the Zhejiang Department of Construction at the time, and distributed to Mr. Tan Zhongkui and Mr. Zhou Junmei. Unfortunately, it was not adopted due to the economic environment at the time, and I still regret it today.

The so-called silk industry operating system means placing all departments related to the silk industry under a large operating body and giving them reasonable treatment, such as raw material policy, production management, trade methods, financial plans, and the improvement of rural economy, improving the education and general cultural level of workers, farmers, and their children, and especially focusing on the concentration of business, increasing production, improving work efficiency, and synthesizing business, that is, simultaneously operating various businesses related to the silk industry, such as making machinery, building banks, insurance, silk spinning, extracting pupa oil for the production of hardware, fuel, and daily necessities, purchasing, and consumer cooperation to reduce production costs and strengthen competitive forces.

6. Ways and methods to revive China's silk industry. The situation of the silk industry has changed greatly from 1928 to the present. In 1928, the silk industry was still in a slump, but it could barely maintain itself. Now, the panic is becoming more and more acute, and silk mills are closing down one after another. Farmers are even considering removing mulberry gardens and planting other crops. We are struggling to maintain it, let alone expand it. In order to restore the old appearance of the silk industry, I would like to offer the following business opinions.

The reasons for the decline of China's silk industry are very complicated, among which the main reason is the world economic panic, but there are special reasons in China, such as the Japanese raw silk's manipulation of the market and exchange rate relations, and the immaturity of technology. If we want to revive the silk industry, we must seek a solution from the entire economy and politics, but this matter is too big and difficult to carry out, so we can only passively deal with the internal problems of the silk industry in order to obtain a solution.

Recently, due to the rapid changes in silk prices, some small-scale factories in the Japanese silk industry have also been shut down. In order to seek an outlet for cocoon production, farmers have organized silk reeling cooperatives, which are the so-called cooperative silk reeling in our country. The benefits of cooperative silk reeling can be divided into the following points: (1) The cocoons produced by farmers can abolish the profit system of general business silk reeling according to the principle of cooperation, so it is possible to increase the price of cocoons. (2) The price of raw cocoons must be calculated according to the average silk price of the whole year, so it is not affected by the change of silk price and can stabilize the operation of the silk industry. (3) The quality of production is closely related to the participants in the production, so it can promote the technological improvement of the silk industry. However, in the past, Japanese cooperative silk reeling was not very developed because the scale was too small, the number of working days in the whole year was too small, and it was in the golden age of business silk reeling. Recently, due to various stimuli, it has been greatly rectified and has achieved a connection in silkworm rearing, silk reeling, and sales, so it can compete with general business silk reeling. If we want to revive the silk industry, we can only choose this way. In our country, the Linong Silk Factory run by Mr. Bu Mutao of Xifengyang, Deqing County, Zhejiang Province, is a model for cooperative silk reeling, but at that time, the factory did not adopt steam engines, the workers' technology was not skilled, and the management was poor, so it not only affected the decline of cocoon prices, but also caused misunderstandings among farmers and did not gain the trust of farmers, so it failed. The second is the Xiaoshan Dongxiang Silk Cooperative, Wuxi Huaxin Silk Cultivation Institute, Hangzhou Weicheng Company, etc. The above factories all adopt the special silkworm rearing cooperative system, but not the thorough cooperative silk reeling, so when the silk price fluctuates violently, there is still a risk of speculation, especially the silk reeling technology affects the low cocoon price, and the settlement of cocoon prices has no accurate method, or the selfishness of the operators is inevitable, and it is inevitable that it cannot obtain the belief of farmers. At present, except for Wuxi Huaxin, the other factories that adopt this system have closed down one after another due to poor business.

The most difficult problem in cooperative silk reeling is to determine the value (in terms of quality), price, and payment method of cocoons. The value of cocoons depends on the amount of cocoon layer, the ease of dissolution (difficult-to-dissolve cocoons directly affect the low production efficiency), and the quality of cocoons. In Japan, the value of cocoons is usually determined by mouth reeling (testing cocoon samples) or special testing methods. The mouth reeling method is to calculate the value of cocoons based on the results of the test reeling, and the special testing method uses instruments for checking the amount of cocoon layer and chemical reactions for testing dissolution to calculate it. Regarding these technical problems, it is impossible to describe them in detail in a few words, so I will not go into details. Although the price must be based on value, it must still be calculated according to the average silk price. The feature is that it is determined based on the average silk price of the whole year or the total average price per dan of silk. Cocoons with uneven quality and value are given a certain increase or decrease. Unlike business silk reeling, which is determined based on the temporary silk price and unreasonable methods, there is absolutely no speculation and danger in cooperative silk reeling. However, what we must pay attention to is the payment method. The poverty of the countryside has reached its extreme, so the need for cash is extremely urgent. Therefore, a part of the cash must be paid during the cocoon production period. In Japan, this prepaid cash is called [temporary crossing money], which means the prepaid amount of the assumed price. The amount is about 70% to 80% of the total cocoon price. The capital of cooperative silk reeling in Japan must be gathered by the personnel participating in cooperative silk reeling, and the central treasury and lending associations of industrial associations can be used to facilitate the turnover of finance. In our country, it is very difficult to gather this capital, and there are very few such organizations except for the Agricultural and Industrial Bank, so government subsidies or methods to guarantee the circulation of finance are necessary to succeed. The following is a draft of the principles for the initial trial implementation of cooperative silk reeling in Jiangsu and Zhejiang.

(1) Use existing factories. In Japan, the factories of combined silk reeling are usually built by farmers who raise funds, but given the current financial situation of the countryside in our country, it is impossible to make this investment, so in order to actively revive the silk industry, we have to use existing factories to make it easier and easier. This factory shall be selected by the Jiangsu and Zhejiang silk authorities in a certain silkworm rearing area, and the nearby silk reeling factory shall be suitable, but for the convenience of trade, the number of silk reeling machines for the initial trial shall be limited to 2,000 to 3,000 machines. If it is successful, it will be gradually increased. The government should also formulate regulations to promote this cooperative silk reeling.

(2) Finance. It is assumed that the designated cooperative silk reeling machine is 2,000 machines, and the average monthly silk reeling is about 450 dan to 550 dan. Each dan needs a advance payment of about 300 yuan. In one or two months, about 1,000 dan of silk reeling is calculated, and the circulating capital is about 300,000 yuan. The government should subsidize or advance loan about 150 yuan per silk machine on average. As for the cocoons produced by farmers, the cash of 70% to 80% of the assumed current price shall be prepaid. The government shall bear the responsibility for guaranteeing the circulation of this cash. However, cooperative silk reeling has no risk of speculation, so the credit can be stable. If the operation is successful, the bank will be happy to lend.

(3) After the establishment of cooperative silk reeling, the Jiangsu and Zhejiang silk authorities shall organize a cooperative silk reeling management committee to supervise financial business, guide cooperative methods and technical improvement, and act as an agent for selling products and promoting the benefits of cooperation.

7. Conclusion. To sum up the above points, cooperative silk reeling has a strong resistance to the changes in silk prices because the price of raw materials is reasonably determined, and has sufficient business possibilities. The financial aspect is stable due to the stable business and the credit is strengthened. Especially since cooperative silk reeling is based on the principle of no profit, as long as it can maintain the current technical level, the price of raw cocoons produced by farmers can be considerably increased. The excellence of farmers' silkworm rearing performance is directly related to farmers' interests, and the workers of cooperative silk reeling are mostly the children of farmers, so it will surely promote the improvement of silkworm rearing and silk reeling technology. At the same time, cooperative silk reeling is to promote technical improvement, so considerable education is given to the farmers and workers under cooperative silk reeling, and the education of farmers' and workers' children is also included, so as to improve the cultural level of the general society. At the same time, in order to closely unite with farmers, cooperative silk reeling must do its best to increase health and entertainment facilities to improve social welfare.

However, in the early days of cooperative silk reeling, the determination of the value and price of raw material cocoons must be accurate and fair in order to increase farmers' favor and avoid misunderstandings. At the same time, technical improvement must be promoted to increase the price of cocoons, and close contact and explanation with farmers must be made to gain farmers' trust and consolidate the foundation of cooperative silk reeling.

Cotton Industry Control Association

Investigation Team Departs Yesterday

The country is divided into three regions and five teams, starting on different routes

Expected to be completed in four months and return to Shanghai to report

The Cotton Industry Control Association of the National Economic Committee organized an investigation team to go to East China, North China, and Central China to start the investigation in order to investigate the national cotton industry situation. The previous report briefly recorded it. It is now known that the investigation team has left yesterday. The details are as follows.

Zonal Investigation

The national investigation is divided into three zones: (1) The East China Zone, with Shanghai as its main base, encompassing cotton mills in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. The Shanghai area is further divided into East Shanghai and West Shanghai zones. (2) The North China Zone, with Tianjin as its main base, encompassing cotton mills in Hebei, Shandong, and Shanxi. (3) The Central China Zone, with Wuhan as its main base, encompassing cotton mills in Hubei, Shashi, and Hunan, Henan, Jiangxi, and Anhui.

Items for Investigation

The investigation items are divided into spinning, weaving, dyeing, finishing, power, factory management, company organization, cost accounting, labor conditions, and statistics.

Investigator Selection

Each group has one leader, appointed from the association's technical specialists. Investigators are appointed from those familiar with the cotton industry factory conditions in each region. For the East China Zone, the group leader is Fu Daoshen, and Wang Zisu; the group members are Hu Shuze, Wang Zhiping, Zhang Angqian, and Su Yanbin. For the Central China Zone, the group leader is Xiao Lunyu; the group members are Liu Dilin and Luo Wuchen. For the North China Zone, the group leader is Jian Guangyu; the group members are Ma Yaoqu, Jiang Fuhai, and Zhu Zhihua. The leader of the National Dyeing and Finishing Factory Investigation Group is Fu Mingjiu; the group members are Li Zhushang, Liu Pengcheng, Qin Zonglu, and Zhu Chuqing. The leader of the Marketing Department Production and Sales Investigation Group is Tong Lüqing; the group members are Zhao Bohua, Zhang Xinmin, Wang Bohua, Zhang Zhenming, Mao Shoufu, Ma Zhuoyun, Yuan Benlong, and Tao Zukai. Statistical investigation: Feng Shuyuan, Zhu Wenhuan, Yu Yipo, etc., totaling over thirty people.

Investigation Period

Each group departed separately yesterday for on-site investigations, which are expected to be completed in four months.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Takes Over Hai Rui and Hai Xiang

Hai Rui Will Serve the Shanghai-Laoyao Route

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company purchased two Norwegian ships and is now taking them over. The Hai Rui has already arrived in Shanghai, and the company has sent a business director to board the ship and take over transportation matters. Details regarding scheduled changes and flag protocols are as follows:

Full Payment of Ship Price

The price of the Norwegian ships Hai Xiang and Hai Rui was paid in six installments. The final payment of 30,000 yuan has been obtained and paid to the Norwegian shipowners by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. Hai Rui was taken over by the company on the 18th of this month, and Hai Xiang was received on the 15th of this month.

Appointment of Personnel

Upon Hai Rui’s arrival in Shanghai, Shi Lianting was appointed by the company as business director, and the personnel of the tally department were also appointed by Mr. Shi. They boarded the ship on the 18th and began their duties. A business director has also been hired for Hai Xiang and will board the ship as soon as it arrives in Shanghai.

Change of Flags

The ship originally flew the Norwegian flag. Now that the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has officially taken over, the ship's smokestack has been painted yellow according to the company's standard to show uniformity. As for the flag, it should be changed to the company's emblem, but it is said that due to time constraints, it will be corrected and changed starting next month.

Details of the Two Ships

Hai Rui has a deadweight of 1,852 tons and is registered at 1,086 tons. Hai Xiang has a deadweight of 1,850 tons and is registered at 1,094 tons. Both were built in 1918, each being 261 feet long and 34 feet 6 inches wide, with fore and aft empty compartments of AP692. The machinery is Triple, with two large boilers using a steam pressure of 180. Each has only one deck. Hai Rui was built by the American Kerr Fluren SB factory, and Hai Xiang was built by Superior SB·OC. Because there is a lot of combined transport cargo from Haizhou, Hai Rui has been assigned to a special Shanghai-to-Laoyao route.

Minister of the Navy

Chen Shaokuan Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning and Went to Nanjing That Evening

Fujian and Xiamen Are Temporarily the Responsibility of Chen Jiliang and Lin Guogeng

Navy Losses Amounted to 500,000 to 600,000, Few Casualties

The Central News Agency reports that Minister of the Navy Chen Shaokuan took the Ninghai warship from Shanghai to Fujian on the 11th at 9 a.m. to preside over naval operations. Fuzhou has now been captured. Because the Fourth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee is opening and Chen is also a member of the Central Executive Committee, he took the original ship again on the 17th and returned to Shanghai from Fujian at 8:30 a.m. yesterday. After disembarking, Chen went to the Jiangnan Shipyard to meet with his subordinates, and then met with reporters from various newspapers to talk in detail about the navy's capture of Fuzhou. Chen himself took the night train to Nanjing last night to attend the Fourth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee. Details are as follows:

Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning and Went to Nanjing That Evening

Minister Chen returned to Shanghai on the Ninghai warship at 8:30 a.m. yesterday and docked at the Gaochangmiao naval pier. Those who went to welcome him included Chen Xunyong, commander of the training fleet, Chen Zaofan, deputy director of the Jiangnan Shipyard, Luo Xuhe, director of the Navy Ordnance Department, Zeng Yijing, director of the Navy Aircraft Manufacturing Office, and Ye Baoqi, battalion commander of the Navy Guard Battalion, and many others. After landing, Minister Chen went to the Jiangnan Shipyard to rest and meet with his subordinates and reporters from various newspapers. At 11 p.m. that night, he took the night train to Nanjing to report to the Central Government on the recapture of Fuzhou and attend the Fourth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee.

Announced the Recapture of Fuzhou

Minister Chen met with reporters from various newspapers at the Jiangnan Shipyard at about 11 a.m. yesterday to announce the recapture of Fuzhou. According to him, he first went to Xiamen and then to Fuzhou, which took a total of eight days. Fuzhou was recaptured on the 16th. Currently, two brigades of naval infantry and many warships are stationed there to maintain order. After entering the city with Commander Chen Jiliang, he not only issued a notice to appease the people, but also declared that he was responsible for protecting the lives and property of foreigners. Therefore, the foreign soldiers who had landed have all withdrawn to their original ships.

Navy Maintains Security in Fujian and Xiamen

Before government administrators and the army arrive, the navy will temporarily maintain security in Fuzhou and Xiamen and handle post-war matters. Currently, the person in charge of Fuzhou is Chen Jiliang, commander of the First Fleet, and the person in charge of Xiamen is Lin Guogeng, commander of the Xiamen Fortress. As for Li Mengbin, commander of the Majiang Fortress, he is still stationed in Mawei. Currently, a total of more than 20 warships are stationed in Fuzhou and Xiamen and have tasks and will not be transferred temporarily. Until Minister Chen left Fuzhou, the army had not yet entered Fuzhou. The situation in Fuzhou and Xiamen has now returned to normal and is quite peaceful.

Two Main Reasons for Retreating from Fuzhou

There are two reasons why the Fujian rebels retreated from Fuzhou this time. The army was pressing forward from the front and the navy was pressing forward from the rear, creating a pincer attack, and the air force was pressing from above, making it difficult for the rebel army to defend. This is one reason. The tax revenue of the pseudo-government has been reduced by more than 300,000 yuan per month since the fall of Xiamen, causing a major economic panic. This is the second reason. With these two major reasons, the Fujian rebels had to abandon Fuzhou and retreat to Zhangzhou and Quanzhou.

The Annihilation of the Rebels is Imminent

After the National Army recaptures Fuzhou, it will definitely take advantage of the victory to pursue and attack Zhangzhou and Quanzhou. The annihilation of the rebels is imminent. As for the rumor that the 19th Route Army will be led and reorganized by Dai Ji, Minister Chen has only seen it in the newspapers and has not heard of it. However, the 19th Route Army has now been defeated. According to Minister Chen's observation, the future result of the 19th Route Army will be that some of them will return to the Central Government, some will become bandits, some will surrender to Guangdong, and some will abandon their guns and seek other livelihoods.

Navy Losses Amounted to 500,000 to 600,000

Since the outbreak of the Fujian Rebellion, the naval institutions in Fujian have been successively occupied, and all the arms and ammunition have been completely plundered. Now that Fuzhou has been captured and the pseudo-government has been eliminated, the naval departments in Fuzhou and Magang have also been taken over one by one. The naval losses have been inspected and found to be 500,000 to 600,000. As for the navy officers and soldiers who disregarded their own safety and attacked Xiamen and Fuzhou, there were of course casualties, but the number was small and has not yet been determined, approximately less than 100. As for the losses suffered by the rebel army, such as the sieges of Lianjiang and Fuzhou, there were many casualties and injuries, and many were captured and disarmed. Currently, the wounded soldiers and prisoners of the rebel army are being held in Fuzhou.

People in the War Zone Urgently Need Relief

The people in the war zone suffered heavy losses in the Fujian Rebellion and suffered extremely painful oppression by the brutal rebels. Minister Chen deeply hopes that the government will provide relief and has sent Commander Li Mengbin to inspect the disaster area for presentation to the Central Government. Minister Chen did not meet with Sa Zhenbing during his stay in Fujian. Sa Zhenbing had nothing to do with this incident.

No Proposals from the Navy at the Plenary Session

Minister Chen is scheduled to go to Nanjing tonight to attend the Fourth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee. As for the discussions at the conference, they will focus on party and government affairs, so Minister Chen has no proposals on the navy to be discussed.

Jiaoji Railway

Combined Transportation Encounters Obstacles

Due to Japanese Merchants’ Opposition

Difficult to Achieve by the End of the Month

The Xinsheng News Agency reported that after the National China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the Ministry of Railways' Combined Transportation Office signed a contract to handle national water-land combined transportation, the Longhai Railway combined transportation has been implemented, and the Jiaoji Railway combined transportation rules have also been negotiated and approved by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's board of directors. It will be implemented on a scheduled basis after the signing of General Manager Liu Hongsheng. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company plans to start at the end of this month, but according to yesterday's exploration of the shipping industry by the Xinsheng News Agency reporter, Qingdao's shipping industry relies entirely on the Jiaoji Railway's freight transportation, which has always been controlled by Japanese merchants. The most ships sailing are the Japanese merchants' Dalian Shipping Co., Ltd., etc., followed by the British merchants Taikoo and Jardine Matheson, and only three Chinese merchants: China Merchants, Zhengji, and Sanbei. Since the Jiaoji Railway was recovered by our country from the Japanese, the redemption price still needs to be paid for four years. Japanese merchants are strongly opposed to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's handling of combined transportation, resulting in obstacles to the future of combined transportation. It is feared that it will be difficult to achieve by the end of this month.

Checking Passengers

Offering Rewards for Arresting Thieves

After the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Puan was robbed and returned to Shanghai, the company is actively rescuing passengers and pursuing pirates. The company has also offered a reward to detect and arrest the pirates in order to crack the case as soon as possible. The follow-up news is recorded as follows:

Offering a Reward of 10,000 Yuan to Arrest Pirates

Liu Hongsheng, general manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, forwarded the Puan's captain's report on the robbery details to the board of directors and the Ministry of Communications. Yesterday, the board of directors issued a notice offering a reward for detecting and arresting pirates, saying that the Puan was robbed on the 15th and nine passengers were taken away from the ship in the Yian Bay area. This unfortunate incident not only affects the national shipping industry but also destroys the patriotism of the Chinese people. In addition to telegraphing the authorities to strictly arrest and rescue, it has been decided that regardless of the community, if they can help solve the case and it is found to be true, they will be rewarded with 10,000 yuan. This notice has been distributed to all branches in Nanhua and ordered to be announced immediately.

Puan Will Open to Qingdao as Usual Today

The Puan is approved to depart from Shanghai to Qingdao at 9:15 a.m. today. The passengers who were robbed are still taking the original ship to Qingdao. The company telegraphed the Qingdao branch yesterday. The goods carried by the ship, except for slightly damaged pieces of cloth and cigarettes, have been notified to the passengers, and there were no other losses. They have been sorted out and the original ship is transporting Qingqi and unloading.

Actively Taking Anti-Theft Measures for Ocean Liners

After the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Yushun was robbed, the shipping department immediately planned anti-theft measures for each ocean liner. It was first decided to add iron fences, increase the number of maritime police, and build silver vaults. The ships included Xinming, Xinfeng, Yushun, Haiyan, Taishun, Guangji, and Jiahe. At that time, the shipping department estimated that it would cost more than 30,000 yuan, which has been gradually equipped. Now that the Puan incident has occurred, the shipping department has further accelerated the construction of anti-theft equipment for each ship that has not been fully equipped, and more armed maritime police have been added to each ocean liner to protect it. Passengers are still required to undergo inspection before boarding to avoid bandits mixing in again.

American Cotton is Selling Poorly in Shanghai

Only 3,000,000 to 4,000,000 Yuan Has Been Sold So Far

The Xinxin News Agency reported that since the American cotton and wheat purchased by our country arrived in Shanghai some time ago, various parties have paid close attention to the sales situation. According to a certain official of the Ministry of Finance, our country used the American cotton and wheat loan of 50,000,000 to purchase wheat for 6,000,000, flour for 4,000,000, and cotton for 40,000,000. Now the cotton and wheat have been purchased and shipped to Shanghai in batches, but the flour has not yet been purchased and shipped, and the purchase cost is higher than that of domestic products, plus transportation costs, which has caused our country a great loss. Checking the Sino-American purchase and transportation procedures, 10% of the price must be paid in advance when ordering, and 5% of the price must be paid when shipping. That is, before the American goods have arrived, we have already paid a considerable price. In other words, we have already incurred such debt. However, the cotton and wheat that have arrived are not selling well because the production of cotton and wheat in various parts of the country is also very abundant this year, and the market price of cotton and wheat has not increased, so the spot goods cannot be sold. So far, only 3,000,000 to 4,000,000 yuan has been sold. Even if all the goods that have arrived are sold, the income will only be 18,000,000 yuan, which is difficult to offset compared with the borrowed debt.

Weining Gunboat Test Run Yesterday

The Weining gunboat, a cruising gunboat used by the Coast Guard Office of the Ministry of the Navy, was still actively under construction after raising its flag on New Year's Day because there were still some scattered projects inside that had not been completed. It has now been fully completed and sailed to Longhua for a test run at 8 a.m. yesterday. The boat's captain, Xu Yuanliang, and the supervisor, Wang Zhiguang, etc., went on board and returned to Gaochangmiao at 1 p.m. It is scheduled to start its maiden voyage to Nanjing next week, and then go to sea for patrol.

Is it appropriate to respectfully request a public decision?

City Chamber of Commerce Telegram to the Ministry of Finance

Extending the Deadline for Domestic Goods in Transit

Merchants' Reasons for Application Should Be Permitted

Exemption from Completing Import Tax Payments

The City Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Nanjing Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating that on the 18th of this month, it received a letter from the Guangbang Silk and Cloth Industry Joint Association, stating that its members, Gong Changhe and Wansheng South, had informed the association that on June 22nd, they had declared to the Zhongxin Heng Customs Broker for loading onto the Taikoo Company's Sichuan ship to Hong Kong for transfer to the Hengfeng Factory in Wuzhou. There were fifteen double packages of twelve-pound English Ball brand fine twill cloth, totaling six hundred pieces, which were entrusted to the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank for exchange to Hong Kong. They were preparing to continue shipping to Wuzhou in accordance with the deadline for domestic goods in transit. However, at that time, Wuzhou was suffering from a major flood, and all commercial activities were completely suspended. In addition, the silver industry was collapsing frequently, and remittances were invisibly suspended. Only after the market had slightly stabilized did they remit funds to continue shipping. Unexpectedly, the goods arrived in Wuzhou on August 25th, exceeding the two-month deadline for domestic goods in transit. The Cangwu Customs required the merchant to pay tax according to the method for overdue domestic goods in transit, treating them as imported goods, and the Jianghai Customs also urged the merchant to pay the domestic goods export tax of 142.79 yuan. The merchant had no choice but to pay the full amount on November 25th. Statistically, the value of the fifteen double packages of fine twill cloth was only over 3,000 yuan, while the Cangwu Customs' supplementary levy of import tax as imported goods was about 2,000 yuan. The merchant's capital is limited, and it has been unable to support itself under the impact of the economic downturn in recent years. If it suffers this punishment, there is no other way but to close down. The merchant has never dared to exceed the deadline for transit in the past. This time, the delay was caused by the special circumstances of the silver industry turmoil and the flood, which was truly a last resort and not an intentional violation of tax regulations. The facts should be fully disclosed, and the Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce should be requested to telegraph the Ministry of Finance to take into account the merchant's difficulties and to quickly instruct the Jianghai and Cangwu Customs to allow them to be treated as domestic goods in order to maintain their capital and continue to operate, which would be a great benefit, etc. The letter was forwarded to the association. The association found that the domestic goods in transit must pass through foreign countries to reach their destination due to transportation relations. The regulations stipulate a two-month deadline. If the deadline is exceeded, import tax must be collected according to the example of imported goods. Whether the stipulation of this two-month deadline is too short, we will not discuss it in depth. However, according to national government orders, if there is a legal deadline for a certain event, if there is a real obstacle, an extension may be allowed, which is not unchangeable. For example, appeals to the court and company registration, although there are legal deadlines, are all allowed to be extended. How can customs duties, which are related to financial administration, be uniquely different? Moreover, transit through foreign countries is a special situation in our country, and since customs duties have been revised many times, transit tax is the lightest, export tax is the next lightest, and import tax is the heaviest. The Hengfeng Textile Factory fine twill cloth transported by the two companies was exported from Shanghai, and the fact that it is not foreign goods is obvious. If the regulations must be strictly adhered to, and an export tax must be supplemented in the place of export in Shanghai if the deadline is exceeded by two months, and an import tax must be levied in the place of sale, then the tax levied on domestic goods in transit from foreign countries is heavier than that on foreign goods, and the transit of domestic goods to the three provinces of Guangdong, Guangxi, and Yunnan through Hong Kong is a common practice. How can market changes and local accidents be predicted? Once the deadline is exceeded, the supplementary tax is more than half of the value of the goods. Merchants will seek profit from their capital, and who would be willing to order goods from Shanghai factories again? This approach is tantamount to suppressing the vitality of domestic goods. In the association's opinion, if there is a real obstacle after the two-month period stipulated in the regulations expires, merchants should be requested to apply for an extension to avoid completing import tax payments in order to maintain the fairness of the law and the circumstances. The Gong Changhe and Wansheng companies in this case have already separately submitted a request to the Customs Administration. The department should be requested to carefully review and order the Customs Administration to allow them to extend the deadline and exempt them from supplementary tax payments, which would be fair and convenient. The Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce respectfully kowtows.

Declaration of the China Youth Anti-Communist League

To Eliminate Red Activities in the Film Industry

The China Youth Anti-Communist League wrote: "Dear Sir, we hereby submit multiple copies of our league's declaration, hoping for your careful consideration and requesting that you generously allocate some space to disclose the declaration in order to arouse the attention of all circles. This is not only the country's fortune but also society's blessing. We respectfully wish you auspicious editing."

Unfortunately, the Chinese film industry was seized by a group of red writers and communists at the beginning of 1933 as a tool for propagating communism and inciting class struggle. The so-called four major film companies – Star, Tianyi, Lianhua, and Yihua – were almost entirely manipulated by them, and their productions were mostly infiltrated with proletarian consciousness. In order to revitalize Chinese national culture and maintain the proper development of the Chinese film industry, we had no choice but to use various means to awaken the Chinese film industry, hoping that they would not be exploited by the Communist Party. However, within the above-mentioned film companies, communist elements are still very active and continue to produce films that propagate red ideas and promote class struggle. Their harm to the country and poisoning of society is especially heinous and unforgivable. At the beginning of 1934, we solemnly make the following declaration to the film industry: (1) Film companies must absolutely not produce films that propagate red ideas, harm the country, depict class struggle, or provoke ethnic animosity. In particular, they must absolutely not confuse proletarian-conscious films with national-conscious films. The depiction of social pathologies and dark sides should also be avoided as much as possible to conform to the purpose of educating society. We also humbly hope that film companies will thoroughly change their style, take the revival of the Chinese nation as the main standpoint of new films, promote production and entrepreneurship, encourage the spirit of struggling hard to overcome the environment, and help improve the country's destiny. (2) Films that are currently being produced or have been produced but have not been publicly released, such as Star's "Twenty-Four Hours in Shanghai" and "Harvest," Lianhua's "Wind," and Yihua's "Golden Age," "Flames," "Flesh Fighting," "National Survival," and "The Wrath of the Chinese Sea," should be automatically deleted and revised before they can be rented and screened. If they cannot be deleted and revised, they should be stopped immediately. (3) Communist films that have already been screened, such as "Three Modern Women," "Torrent," "Maternal Love's Light," "Salt Tide," "Oppression," "Vanilla Beauty," "Dawn," "Women's Cry," and "City Night," must be automatically deleted and cut in their entirety. Anything that endangers national unity, provokes class antagonism, or propagates communist ideas must be thoroughly removed. (4) Tian Han (i.e., Chen Yu), Shen Duanxian (i.e., Ding Zhiyi), Qian Xingcun, Mao Dun, Shen Xicen, Lou Jiannan, and Xu Xixingzhi are all red writers. Companies must absolutely not use scripts written by them, and those who hold directorial positions must immediately have their employment contracts terminated. (5) Starting this year, for films listed in the second and third clauses, if the film companies do not modify them and formally announce the corrections in various newspapers and periodicals, no cinema in the country, regardless of location, may rent or screen them. Those who deliberately resist will be bombed with bombs. (6) Film publications and film supplements in major newspapers should also be particularly vigilant and should no longer publish film reviews that promote red ideas, otherwise they will also be served with bombs. In addition to submitting the above-mentioned principles to the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government Military Affairs Commission, and the party headquarters of various provinces and municipalities for assistance in banning them, we have also issued orders to the local branches throughout the country to implement them thoroughly. At the same time, we have strictly ordered the investigation and action departments to immediately carry out severe punishment once they are discovered – punishing film publications, production companies, and cinemas that violate public opinion and endanger the country. Finally, we know that the reason why proletarian films have been rampant in recent years is that the members of the Nanjing Film Censorship Committee should bear a very heavy responsibility. Some people say that these committee members may be "insane" and blind for encouraging red ideas so much. In any case, they deserve the blame and there is no doubt about it. It is heard that a large portion of the films they have approved have been ordered by the Jiangxi Provincial Government not to be screened within Jiangxi Province. It is also heard that the central government has warned them and is conducting an investigation. Therefore, we will temporarily take a wait-and-see attitude to wait for the government to punish them quickly. If the Film Censorship Committee again approves the fact that a red film has been discovered, regardless of whether it is out of favoritism or blindness, its eyes will be gouged out to show a warning. This declaration is hereby solemnly made, hoping for the understanding of all circles. The Council of the China Youth Anti-Communist League, January of the 23rd year of the Republic of China.

Alkali Fate: Falling to Death from the Eighth Floor

American Pilot and Wife Constantly Quarrel

His Wife First Threw Down Two Children and Then Jumped Down Herself

An American pilot, Grochu, is currently employed as a driver for China National Aviation Corporation, living with his wife and two children (the elder seven years old, the younger five) in a newly built eight-story western-style public residence at the intersection of Route Petain and Route Cohen in the French Concession. The relationship between the couple is usually very poor, and they often quarrel. Yesterday morning, they had another dispute over a trivial matter, and Grochu went to the company to work. Unexpectedly, Grochu's wife had thoughts of厭世. At 5:45 pm, she led her two children to the highest rooftop on the eighth floor, first throwing the two children down, and then following suit and jumping down herself. All three had their brains splattered and died on the spot. After the nearby police found out, they immediately reported to the police station, and the head of the station ordered detectives to rush to the scene for investigation. They will notify the US Consulate to handle the matter.

Twelfth Session of the YMCA

Important Issues of the General Assembly

To be Held at St. John's University on January 23

The 12th National Congress of the Chinese Christian Youth Association will be held at St. John's University on January 23, as reported in the previous newspaper. The holding of this meeting will have a great impact on the work direction of the Youth Associations throughout the country in the next three years. The content of its important issues is listed below:

Agricultural and Industrial Undertakings

Youth Associations throughout the country are either located in important industrial centers such as Shanghai and Tianjin, or in important rural centers such as Suzhou and Wuhu. Therefore, the National Congress has specifically put forward the proposal of agricultural and industrial undertakings so that Youth Associations in various places can take these two tasks as their important work. At the conference, methods of engaging in and promoting labor work will be discussed, and Youth Associations in various places that already have labor work will be invited to report on their work achievements for other Youth Associations to learn from. In terms of rural work, it will be discussed whether Youth Associations should promote rural work with urban Youth Associations as the center or establish rural Youth Associations separately, and what kind of rural work Youth Associations should engage in should also be determined. As for the method of training rural cadres, it is also one of the issues.

Social Work

All kinds of undertakings handled by urban Youth Associations are part of social work, and at this conference, they will all be evaluated to see what contributions they have made to society. In order to achieve good results, a Social Work Committee has been organized before the meeting to study it. The committee believes that the social work of the Youth Association should be re-determined according to the doctrine, the times, and the national conditions, taking the new social order as the basis, seeking profound and concrete awareness, educational methods, civilian nature, and effectiveness to penetrate into the lives of the masses. In short, its work should be purely for the welfare of the masses.

Student Affairs

There are more than one hundred and twenty school Youth Associations scattered in various schools, and most of the urban Youth Associations in various places are located in educational centers. Therefore, student affairs is also an important issue of this National Congress. This topic has also been researched by a separate committee before the meeting. The old organization of Youth Associations in various schools focused on rigid departments and seemed unable to effectively meet the needs of the school. Therefore, the future organization should focus on lively and vibrant small fellowships, and the lives of the members of the school Youth Association should also establish standards for training. The training of students and staff in office skills and the recruitment and training of student cadres are also one of the issues of this National Congress.

It is also heard that the convening of this National Congress in Shanghai has attracted the attention of various circles in Shanghai. China Travel Service and Shanghai Bank will set up offices at St. John's University during the meeting. The National Film Education Promotion Office will screen educational films for representatives during the meeting for publicity purposes. National goods companies will also send staff to distribute gifts to the representatives of the National Youth Association. At the same time, a National Youth Association Work Exhibition will also be held.

Second District Police Department

Cracking Down on a Large Number of Thieves

Transferred from Kunshan

And Arrested in Shanghai

Li, the district chief of the Second District of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, learned that a robbery had occurred in the Changtai Cigarette and Paper Store opened by Mr. Xia in No. 18, West Gate, Lane 35, Gaochang Temple, within the jurisdiction of this district, and at the same time, the Wanxing Cigarette and Paper Store opened by Mr. Lin Shi in No. 1, Chengzhi Lane, opposite, was also robbed. In addition, the home of Cao Musheng (who is a member of the Security Corps) in Xiaomuqiao, Longhua Road, was robbed by bandits of 450 silver dollars, 74 small silver dollars, and clothing. In addition, the Dacheng Cigarette and Paper Store opened by Mr. Zhu Xikun in No. 457, Damuqiao, was robbed of silver dollars. For the above cases, District Chief Li strictly ordered Liu Shaoqing, the leader of the detective team stationed in the district, to order detectives to purchase leads, which have been solved. The details are recorded as follows:

Process of Arrest

At about 8 pm on the 12th of this month, Liu Shaoqing, the leader of the team, ordered detective Lu Lingen to report secretly that he had seen the thief Shang Ziqin at No. 81, Longhua Road. At that time, the detective was unable to return to the district to report, so he immediately reported to the patrol police nearby for assistance in arresting the thief Shang Ziqin. After questioning, Shang confessed that his accomplices Li Degui and Wei Caifeng were hiding in the Tofu Shop in Sanyuan Street, Shiqiang Town, Kunshan City, and that the pistol was also hidden in that place. District Chief Li and Team Leader Liu reported to Wen Hongen, Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, and Lu Ying, Captain of the Detective Team, separately, and prepared a letter to the Kunshan County Government. Team Leader Liu Shaoqing was still ordered to lead detectives Fang Lingen, Shi Chunlin, Gu Rusheng, Cheng Peizhang, Wang Gengsheng, and Zhou Jizhen to hold the document on the 13th of this month and go to Kunshan to meet with the police officers of the county government to secretly go to the above-mentioned location. Li Degui and Wei Caifeng were arrested on the spot and taken to Shanghai for questioning. They confessed that there was a pistol hidden in a mud cave under the bed in the bedroom, etc. On the 17th of this month, the original detectives Fang Lingen, etc. went to Kunshan again to retrieve a six-inch white pistol with the number 38245, three bullets, and a gun clip from Xu Mingjiu, a suspect (Xu is the owner of a tofu shop and is a gentleman in the town. All the partners used by the shop are from Hefei, Anhui, so there is this suspicion) and took them to Shanghai to be questioned. On one side, District Chief Li ordered Team Leader Liu to lead detectives Cheng Peizhang, Yang Jinchen, Gu Rusheng, and Shi Chunlin to take Wei and others to the Sixth District to meet with the chief and police of the Second Sub-Office of the district to arrest Xu Chuanliang (i.e., Xu Wu) and his mistress Xu Liu at No. 37, Xinsen Lane, Hongqiao Road. After questioning in the district, at about 2 am today, the original detectives were sent again to take the suspect to arrest Wang Xinyun at No. 26, Houjiazhai. After questioning in the district, at about 8 am on the 17th, detective Fang Lingen received a report from an informant, Lu Desan, and the detectives and patrol police arrested the thief Zhang Chengyi at the railway side of the South Railway Station, and Zhang also confessed the suspect Hu Guoqing, who was taken to the district for interrogation.

Confessions in Pieces

According to the confession of the thief Li Degui arrested in Kunshan, he first partnered with Wang Degui and others to rob Xu Dayuan's home at No. 6, Songsheng Lane, Kangqu Road, Jumen Road. He firmly claimed that the pistol was stolen by Yang Haishan from a milk shed in the French Concession. Wei Caifeng confessed that he partnered with Huang Siqiaozi, Zhang Chengyi, etc. to rob a grocery store in a bungalow at the intersection of Xiaomuqiao and Xietu Road, and robbed the cigarette and paper store in Damuqiao. Xu Chuanliang (Xu Wu) confessed that the robbery case on Hongqiao Road was indeed a conspiracy, but he firmly denied the other cases. Xu Liu confessed that she did not send a pistol to Zhang Chengyi on his behalf or on behalf of her husband. Wang Xinyun confessed that she had been making a living by weaving cloth and did not dare to be a bandit. Zhang Chengyi also claimed that he partnered to rob a pharmacy near the Rihui Bridge and a cigarette and paper store next to it, and robbed Cao Musheng's home at No. 48, Xiaomuqiao, of 450 yuan, and robbed a cigarette and paper store on the south side of the railway. According to the suspect Xu Mingjiu, he has been doing business in Kunshan. Although the person named Wei is from the same hometown, he really does not know that they have committed illegal acts. He asks for leniency and asks to check to know the truth. Hu Guoqing confessed that he used to make a living by delivering opium and collecting flower parties, and that he had never been involved in robberies.

Ages and Origins of the Suspects

After District Chief Li questioned the above-mentioned suspects one by one, he ordered Team Leader Liu to send detectives Fang Lingen and others to the French Concession to meet with the Songshan Road police station to retrieve the stolen goods from the Xieda Pawnshop, etc. Except for one Huang Siqiaozi who has been arrested and sent to the Sixth District, all the fugitives Wang Xuegui, Xiaoshandong, Xiaowang, Yang Haishan, etc. are still ordered to be arrested by the detectives separately. The suspects who have been reported to the General Bureau for questioning are recorded as follows: Thief Shang Ziqin, 25 years old, Hefei, Anhui; Li Degui, 38 years old, Hefei, Anhui; Wei Caifeng (Yonghai), 32 years old, Hefei; Zhang Chengyi, 28 years old, Hefei; Xu Chuanliang (Xu Wu), 32 years old, Hefei; Xu Liu, 31 years old, Hefei; Suspect Hu Guoqing, 27 years old, Hefei; Wang Xinyun, 25 years old, Hefei; Xu Mingjiu, 38 years old, Hefei.

Novelty

Barge Acting as Gambling Den

Yelling and Shouting in the Huangpu River

Police Arrive to Round Up All

According to Lu Ying, the leader of the detective squad of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, based on information from Chen Caifu, a detective foreman, there is a notorious rogue from Chongming named Wang Chongfu (age 40) in the Shanghai's Nanshi, Shiliupu Ning Shao Wharf area, who colludes with accomplices from Nanjing, Bu Hongsheng, and from Ningbo, Le Aliu and Chen Afa, to entice gamblers to gather on the barge of Gu Aer (age 45) from Yancheng, to gamble and collect a commission. Every night, they gamble by shaking dice and the stakes are quite high. Wang and his gang profit handsomely from this. After Lu Ying verified the information, he immediately instructed the foreman to lead a large number of detectives, together with Zhu Haishan, the captain of the water patrol team in charge of the area, and dispatched Deputy Captain Li Chenghua and several police officers to take a patrol launch to the No. 3 Garbage Wharf in Nanshi around 5 PM the night before. Approaching the barge, they could already hear the gamblers yelling and shouting from outside the boat. The detectives then rushed into the front and rear cabins. When the gamblers saw the detectives, they all tried to jump into the river to escape, causing chaos. The officers arrested the gambling ringleader Wang Chongfu, the boat owner Gu Aer, and other gamblers, including Bu Hongsheng, Xu Ziqing, Qin Kaopeng, Shi Ruilin, Li Guangli, Zhu Ahu, Chen Agen, Zhang Afa, and a total of twenty-five people. They seized gambling equipment such as shaking pots, dice, money boards, small iron boxes, and gambling money of forty dollars in silver and sixty-six cents in small coins on the spot. They then took the team and transferred the case to the Third Section for handling.

Domestic Products

Investigation of Light Bulbs

Electrical Appliance Manufacturing Association Takes Responsibility for Guarantee

Since Japanese counterfeit light bulbs flooded into Shanghai after the import tax was lowered, unscrupulous merchants in this city have disguised these light bulbs as domestic products to deceive their fellow countrymen, making it impossible for buyers to distinguish them. After several days of thorough investigation by this reporter, and a detailed inquiry with the Electrical Appliance Manufacturing Association of this city, it is known that the truly domestic light bulbs that the association can responsibly guarantee include: Ya Pu Er brand, Jingji brand, and San Hai brand from the Ya Pu Er Factory; Hua Tong brand and Feiji brand from the Hua Tong Factory; Hua De brand from the Hua De Factory; Ya Er Deng brand from the Ya Er Deng Factory; Hua Demen brand and China Commander brand; Fu An brand from the Fu An Factory; Yueguang brand from the Xinguanghua Factory; Zhongguo, Yuguo, Huoche, Jishi, Feiergu, Washington, and Wufu brands from the Zhongguo Factory; and Biao Zhun brand from the Shanghai Factory. Those who have not been examined and approved by the Electrical Appliance Manufacturing Association are not allowed to join the association, and it is hoped that buyers everywhere will pay attention.

Foreigner Defrauds Huge Sum

Forging Check

Cashing Out Funds

The Continental Daily reports that someone, likely a foreigner, forged an Anglo-American Tobacco Company check for a six-figure sum this week and cashed it at the Mercantile Bank. The police are currently searching for the person everywhere. Bank staff did not initially notice anything until yesterday when they received another check for over 100,000 yuan, signed by a senior executive of the Anglo-American Tobacco Company. Suspecting something was amiss, they inquired with the company and were shocked to learn that both the check cashed a few days ago and the check presented yesterday were forged. It is still unknown whether the check was forged by the signatory himself or someone else. According to Anglo-American Tobacco Company staff, the first check was countersigned by a foreigner who had deposited 800 yuan in the bank a few days before the exchange. The forged signature was said to be very similar to the real one, making it difficult to detect. According to police sources, the person must be familiar with the true signature method. A thorough investigation is underway in hopes of apprehending the criminal as soon as possible.

Ship's Receipt

Must Not Be Altered or Annotated

Jianghai Customs Notice Promulgated

The General Affairs Section of the Jianghai Customs issued a notice yesterday regarding the matter that the declared consignor on the ship's receipt must not alter or annotate it without authorization. The notice stated that after the Customs had released the goods listed on the ship's receipt, the declared consignor often changed the contents without authorization. It is hereby warned that the ship's receipt is a type of official document of the Customs. In the future, if any unauthorized alteration or annotation is discovered without the approval of the Customs, a fine will be imposed immediately. If it is a registered customs broker, in addition to the fine, the business license will be temporarily suspended or revoked. All merchants should be aware of this. Registered customs brokers should pay particular attention to this notice.

Postal Parcel Rates Temporarily Postponed

At the Railway Intermodal Transport Conference, the Ministry of Railways considered that the basic postage rate for postal items was too low to cover the railway transportation costs. It was proposed that the Ministry of Railways inform the Ministry of Communications to review and appropriately increase the rate to maintain railway operations. It was decided that all postal parcels and packages would be charged according to railway parcel rates. According to the Postal Administration, the railway's proposed increase in postal parcel rates was intended to benefit railway operations. However, the Ministry of Communications and the Postal Administration were unable to fully agree due to various reasons and requested a temporary postponement. Therefore, the Ministry of Railways has now decided to temporarily postpone the increase in postal parcel rates.

Shanghai Ferry Opens Service to Wusong

Service Starts on the 25th of This Month

The Shanghai Ferry Company decided to extend its existing routes to Wusong during the summer of last year to facilitate transportation between Shanghai and Wusong. The construction of the ferry terminal at the old site of the pier on Wusong Town Outer Ma Road has now been completed. It is known that the terminal has been completed and will officially start service on the 25th of this month. From 7:00 AM to 5:00 PM, a ferry will depart every hour. The Wusong and Shanghai Nanjing Road Bund stations will depart on the hour. All stations along the line, such as Xidu, Qingning Temple, Donggou, Gaoqiao, and Guanghua, can be stopped at. The fare between Wusong and Shanghai is 22 cents for second class, 48 cents for first class, and 96 cents for special class. Within the first five days of service, the fare from Wusong to all stations will be discounted by half. The capacity of the ferry is quite large and it can also carry cargo at a very low price. Merchants from Wusong who go to Shanghai to purchase goods can transport them by ferry, which is more convenient than before. It is also learned that, to facilitate passengers from Baoshan and Yanghang, the Shanghai-Tai Long-Distance Bus Company has decided to extend the bus routes from Wusong to Baoshan and Wusong to Yanghang to the Wusong ferry terminal, in accordance with the original plan, and to coordinate with the ferry schedule.

City News

▲ Relief for the Weak and Cold: People with weak bodies often feel cold in their hands and feet when winter comes. This is because their blood volume is insufficient, only enough to circulate in the torso and unable to reach the limbs. Renzao Zilai Xue (Artificial Self-Generating Blood), produced by Wuzhou Pharmacy, is a well-recognized blood tonic for decades. Those who suffer from cold hands and feet should take it regularly to promote blood circulation. The lack of sunlight due to wearing heavy clothes and staying indoors is also a major cause of weakness in the cold season. [Wuzhou Emulsion Cod Liver Oil] and [Earth Brand Malt Extract Cod Liver Oil] are rich in vitamins and are excellent preparations of cod liver oil. They should be taken regularly in this cold season to supplement the lack of sunlight.

▲ *Yaojiang Poetry Anthology* Presented to All Circles: The *Yaojiang Poetry Anthology* in eight volumes was compiled by Xie Peiqing, a *xiaolian* (recommended scholar) from Yuyao. It is a general collection of Yao poetry, founded by Mr. Huang Lizhou, covering from the Southern Qi Dynasty to the end of the Ming Dynasty, called *Yaojiang Lost Poems*. It was continued by Ni Xiaoye and Zhang Luoshan in the early Qing Dynasty. This compilation continues from the early Qing Dynasty to the present, following the examples of Ni and Zhang. It does not include those who are still alive. It includes a total of 518 poets, with 3,500 poems. It is also a literary record of the Yaojiang region in one dynasty. It is planned to be widely circulated and distributed to all circles. Any library or reading room can send a letter with a seal to request it. Weather Report

At 4:30 PM yesterday, the Xujiahui Observatory in Shanghai telegraphed that the Shandong cold air mass and the weather here were clear and cold, which is consistent with the season. The wind was strong. There was rain in the area south of Ma'an Island and along the coast of the South China Sea. The wind in the Yangtze River basin came from the southwest to the northwest. There were reports of cyclones and rain near Japan and the Ogasawara Islands due to the low pressure passing through and heading northeast and east. Also, in the 24 hours before 3 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 42.3 degrees and the lowest was 23.7 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 40.8 degrees and the lowest was 30.7 degrees.

Letters to the Editor

To the Esteemed Editor: In the local news column of your newspaper on January 14th, there was a news item stating that our factory "continues to use enemy goods without repentance." After reading it, we were shocked and horrified to find that it was completely untrue. Since the September 18th Incident, our factory has never purchased enemy goods. We are not only innocent in our conscience, but it is also well known to our colleagues. As for the enemy goods purchased by Xiangtai before the September 18th Incident and not yet sold, they were disposed of in accordance with the resolution of the Iron Industry Association on the handling of enemy goods, and our factory was entrusted to melt the goods on their behalf. Our factory refused early on, which was also well known to the association. This matter concerns the reputation of our factory and it is difficult to remain silent. We hereby request that your newspaper publish this letter in the letters to the editor column to clarify the truth and express our gratitude. Sincerely, Xiangmeng Foundry, January 19th.

To the Esteemed Editor: I am writing to express my surprise at the news in the local news column of your newspaper regarding a "Hundred Embroidery Competition to be held by our organization in early spring." After investigation, our country has no such competition planned. We hereby correct this to avoid misunderstandings. We hope that this letter will be published to prevent public confusion. Sincerely, Shanghai Municipal Zoo, January 19th.
