Special Article

The Crossroads of the Japanese Nation by Wu Tiecheng

Editor's Note: This article was written by Mayor Wu Tiecheng for the Japanese Dentsu News Agency. The original manuscript was translated into Japanese and published in the agency's newly built memorial special issue (Special Issue on the Pacific Ocean Problem). It is a sincere and earnest admonition to the Japanese nation and a significant work in the international community. We have obtained the original manuscript from Mr. Wu and are publishing it for our readers.

— Editor's Note

[The alliance and friendship between China and Japan can guarantee peace in the Eastern Hemisphere.] The development of the mainland is China's responsibility. [In the future, I only hope that we trust each other... to solve the Indian problem. Once the Indian problem is solved, all colored people in the world will be able to revive. Japan should not worry about not having immigration and trade destinations after this achievement. It should never make the foolish strategy of invading China.] [Absolute guarantee of the mainland, and the full development in the United States and Australia is the right path for the survival and development of the Japanese nation.]

These are the heartfelt words of Japanese Gui Taro to the Chinese revolutionary leader, Mr. Sun Yat-sen (see Dai Jitao's *On Japan*, page 97).

Gui Taro was the most powerful and far-sighted military and politician in Japan. He formed a cabinet three times, serving for almost eight years. Since Japan has had a cabinet system, no one has served as prime minister for so long. When Gui was in office, he first allied Japan, a small emerging country, with the world's most powerful empire (Great Britain), causing Britain to abandon its century-old policy of glorious isolation, both to enhance its international status and to strengthen its national defense. Then, he defeated the world's largest continental empire (Russia), sweeping away the psychology of the world's powers despising Eastern nations and arousing a new wave of world national revolution. Since the Meiji Restoration in Japan, no one has been able to establish such amazing achievements for his country. Gui's loyalty to the country, the greatness of his vision, the excellence of his knowledge, and the brilliance of his achievements all led him to say these words. He naturally had extraordinary insights and indelible truths. When the Japanese people recall the martyrs and remember the legacy, they should reflect on what the national policy should be today.

In all fairness, the rise of the Japanese nation is indeed a unique feature of modern history, and the spirit of its people's struggle, sacrifice, integrity, and responsibility for the country and society is something that our Chinese nation cannot match. Chinese and Japanese cultures are thousands of years apart. When Chinese culture was in its golden age, the Japanese people were still in the primitive state of cave dwelling. However, due to the development of their national ambition and the power of assimilation, they first integrated various material and spiritual civilizations imported from Korea, China, and India to meet the needs of their lives, established the foundation of their national culture, and completed the organization of their national society. Then, they embraced the new era of European and Western forces invading the East, accepted European and Western science and culture, and created the foundation of their strength today, gaining an advanced position among the Eastern nations. Looking at modern history, there has never been a nation that has developed as quickly as the Japanese nation. If the Japanese nation can base its development on its ambition and strive to develop along the path of coexistence and co-prosperity for mankind, then its contribution to human culture will be immeasurable.

Examining the driving force behind the historical development of the Japanese nation, one cannot but trace back to the achievements of the Tokugawa era. The Tokugawa era was the heyday of the development of Chinese philosophical thought in Japan. The reason why the Japanese nation was able to break away from the barbaric state of tribal struggle, promote the development of its civil rights, unify its political organization, and even establish the foundation of its modern nation cannot but be attributed to the Chinese philosophical ideas of "benevolence" and "great unity." Those who talk about the Meiji Restoration in Japan often overlook this historical relationship, and the Japanese people also seem unable to recognize the foundation of their national cultural development, so that the orthodoxy of this culture is gradually suppressed by Japan's traditional theocratic historical theory and narrow-minded national psychology, and eventually despise China, blindly follow Europe and the United States, are greedy and insatiable, kill each other, and are obsessed with medieval militarism, thinking that the business of the world is only about force. In fact, they are trapped in the last fate of imperialists. Today's Japanese politicians generally lack far-sighted plans and superb insights. They often have no time to consider the future of the world, the future of the Eastern nations, and how China and Japan can coexist and co-prosper. They also fail to recognize where the true path of the Japanese nation lies. All day long, they are anxious and afraid, thinking that China's unification, China's liberation, and China's self-strengthening will hinder Japan's development and hinder the life of the empire. Therefore, [on the one hand, they loudly tell the world that China is not unified, and on the other hand, they insist on pursuing their policy of obstructing China's unification] (as stated in Gu Weijun's speech at the League of Nations). They do not think that the Chinese nation follows its spirit of loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, love, trustworthiness, justice, peace, and royal culture, treating others generously and practicing good faith and harmony. For thousands of years, although it has been the only great power in East Asia, it has never invaded land or destroyed any nation. It is the greatest guarantee of peace in East Asia. The Tokyo General Staff Headquarters and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs do not lack brilliant talents, but unfortunately, they are all blinded by subjective prejudices and misled by current interests, so they specialize in the inferior strategy of invading China. They do not know that China's development [can guarantee the alliance and friendship between China and Japan and can guarantee peace in East Asia] (as stated by Japan's Gui Taro). This is not only China's misfortune, but it will also bring infinite disaster to the Japanese nation.

Japan proclaims to the world that the reason why the Japanese have no choice but to invade Manchuria is that it is their lifeline, which can solve their economic problems. We will temporarily abandon all feelings of resentment and any political issues, and focus on studying the facts and establishing economic arguments. We will also see that the Japanese people's views are fallacious. Common people think that Manchuria, whether directly or indirectly, can solve Japan's population problem. Those who are not familiar with Manchuria's economic situation think that Manchuria is the direct outlet for Japan's huge annual population increase. Or they think that although Manchuria cannot absorb many Japanese people, it can also promote Japan's further industrialization and maintain a larger population. Manchuria can supply Japan with a lot of food and raw materials, and at the same time, it is also a market for its surplus goods. This kind of thinking has penetrated into the minds of the general public, but what is the reality? We should calm down and conduct objective research on the facts. First, from the perspective of the population problem, the Japanese people are not accustomed to large-scale immigration. Second, the Japanese people's living standards are higher, and they cannot compete with the local Chinese people on a large scale. Next, from the perspective of trade, in the years before the outbreak of the Sino-Japanese dispute, Japan's exports to Manchuria only accounted for more than 8% of its total exports, and its imports from Manchuria accounted for about 70% of its total imports. Therefore, in reality, Japan's largest customers and suppliers are not Manchuria. Furthermore, although Manchuria is very rich in agricultural and mineral products, it has no important relationship with the lives of the Japanese people. The only most important agricultural product that Japan imports from Manchuria has always been soybeans. However, soybeans are mainly used as fertilizer. Japanese people have recently become more fond of chemical fertilizers, so the demand for soybeans will inevitably decrease. As for corn, sorghum, and other grains, the import has not been very large. Although rice is Japan's only important food, Manchuria produces very little rice. Cotton is unable to obtain high profits due to its poor quality. According to Japanese expert surveys, wool needs to be improved for 30 years before it can be supplied to the Japanese people. In terms of mineral products, Japan produces a lot of coal and can supply itself with a surplus. Geologists and mineral experts believe that Manchuria's known iron ore is unsuitable for supplying effective large-scale steel mills due to its low iron content. Japan's iron production is very fast, and its headquarters only consumes one-tenth of its iron production. Wood only accounts for 1% of its total imports and is not needed by Japan. All these arguments are based on the objective research results of modern economics authority Dr. B. Dorfman (Professor at the University of California, USA). Following this objective and scientific argument, we can know that [Manchuria is the lifeline of the Japanese nation] and that [Manchuria can solve Japan's economic problems] are inconsistent with the facts and are only excuses for Japanese ambitious warlords to use force and deceptive terms for Japanese political bureaucrats to deceive the world. It can be seen that Manchuria is not Japan's lifeline. The Japanese invasion of Manchuria is actually the most unprofitable inferior strategy.

Since the Japanese people chanted scorched-earth diplomacy and invaded China, the financial, financial, shipping, factories, commerce, and society have been greatly affected internally, and the international status has continued to decline and the diplomatic front has become increasingly isolated externally (Note). Although the European and American powers were constrained by the economy and could not impose military sanctions, the economic war has been urgently launched, such as India's increase in tariffs and South Africa's restrictions on imports. As for the increase in the construction of warships by various countries, the vertical and horizontal blades all implicitly indicate that the tragic disaster of the world will break out soon. However, the crisis of the Japanese nation is not starting today. After the Russo-Japanese War, the Japanese people flapped their wings and crowed, celebrating the development of their national fortune. They did not know that they would be attacked from both sides and could not rest easy. When the European War broke out, the Japanese once again greatly benefited from the fisherman's profit. However, after the Washington Conference, the songs of Chu rose up on all sides, and the diplomatic front became increasingly dangerous. Following this historical lesson and reasoning, it can be seen that success and failure are two sides of the same coin, not absolute nouns. There is a Chinese proverb that says [If the old man on the border loses his horse, how do you know it is not a blessing]. However, the Japanese people's wisdom is not enough to understand this. They must forcibly swallow and plunder, causing themselves suffering. They think that China is weak and backward and must be conquered by force. However, from a historical point of view, since the cession of Taiwan, Japan has still spent more than ten years and countless military and financial resources to quell the resistance of the aborigines, who are less than three million and have no culture or history, and still failed to convince them. Furthermore, from the current world situation, since the League of Nations Covenant and the Kellogg-Briand Pact were signed, most observers believe that the above two covenants are nothing less than a major revolution in human thought, rather than the result of any accidental impulse or unconscious emotion. If we go back to the source, the two covenants are products of the needs of the times and a manifestation of a kind of self-consciousness. If mankind does not take a new step, modern civilization will be sentenced to death and be on the verge of death. Under the current organization of the world, it is absolutely impossible to continue to recognize cruel wars, along with their increasing destructive power, as a normal tool to benefit human life… In this whole world, regardless of East, West, South, or North, war should be illegal. War should no longer be the source of rights. War should no longer be the principle from which national obligations, rights, and actions arise.]

(Stimson's Kellogg-Briand Pact speech) Therefore, Japan's current national policy is not only inconsistent with the principles shown by its history, but also contrary to the trend of modern world evolution. If it still relies on its reckless courage and does not wake up early, it will inevitably fall into a fork in the road in the principle of human evolution, and the misfortune of the Japanese nation will be even more unbearable to imagine.

(Note) (Mori Kaku, a fierce general of the Seiyukai, questioned Uchida in the parliament and said that since the recognition of the Manchurian State has been decided, Japan must have the determination to break the boat and go to it. We should be aware that international relations, especially the relations between the United States, Japan, China, and Japan, will be worse than before. The government has some views on how to deal with the changes in the international situation and how to develop Japan's position in the international economic community as a result of the recognition (of the Manchurian State). As a result of the recognition (of the Manchurian State), has the government also prepared to deal with the drastic changes in national relations that will occur between China, the United States, Japan, and other countries? (See Hideo Nomura's "The Circumstances of Foreign Minister Hirota's Inauguration" in the October issue of *Chuo Koron*)

[China and Japan are the largest nations in East Asia. China and Japan are the driving forces behind the national independence movement in Asia.

[Europeans use military force and culture to oppress us Asians, so we Asians cannot progress. This kind of culture that uses military force to oppress people is called hegemony in our Chinese ancient language. Therefore, European culture is hegemonic culture. But we Orientals have always despised hegemonic culture. There is another kind of culture that is better than hegemonic culture. The essence of this culture is benevolence, justice, and morality. This kind of culture that uses benevolence, justice, and morality is to influence people, not to oppress people. It is to make people cherish virtue, not to make people grow in power. This kind of culture that makes people cherish virtue is called the royal way in our Chinese ancient language. Therefore, Asian culture is the royal way culture. Since the development of material civilization in Europe and the rise of hegemony, the morality of countries around the world has been declining every day. Even several countries in Asia have also declined a lot. Recently, European and American scholars who have paid a little attention to Oriental culture have gradually realized that although the material civilization of the Orient is not as good as that of the West, the morality of the Orient is much better than that of the West.

[In this world we are in now, what should we use as the foundation to create our Pan-Asianism? We should use our inherent culture as the foundation. We should talk about morality, benevolence, and justice. Benevolence, justice, and morality are the good foundations of our Pan-Asianism. With these good foundations, we also need to learn European science. Learning from Europe does not mean learning from Europe to eliminate other countries and oppress other nations.

[If we want to talk about Pan-Asianism, we want to restore the status of Asian nations. We can only unite the nations of various parts of Asia, with benevolence, justice, and morality as the foundation. The entire Asian nation will be very powerful.

[Your Japanese nation has obtained both the hegemonic culture of Europe and the United States and the essence of the royal way culture of Asia. From now on, whether you will be the dog of the Western hegemons or the guardian of the Eastern royal way for the future of world culture is up to you, the Japanese people, to carefully consider.]

This is the gist of Mr. Sun Yat-sen's speech on Pan-Asianism at the Kobe Higher Girls' School and five groups including the Kobe Chamber of Commerce on November 28, 1924. I still remember that when the speech was given, the Japanese people were so moved by Mr. Sun's sincerity that they were moved to tears. China and Japan are countries of the same language and the same race, brotherly countries. In terms of each other's relationship, the people of both countries should have joined hands and worked together to develop the future of both countries. However, since the Meiji Restoration in Japan, this slogan has never become a reality. Is this truly due to the incompatibility of the interests of the two countries, or is it due to the errors in the strategies of the Japanese authorities?

The media is the expression of social justice. The Dentsu News Agency has a long history of advocating public opinion. I am humiliated to solicit articles based on the motives of loving Japan, loving the Eastern nations, and loving the people of the world. I will use a frank and straightforward attitude to give my most sincere advice. There should be many insightful people in the Dentsu News Agency. I hope they will recognize the duties of the media and continue to fight for justice, point out the fork in the road for the Japanese nation, and jointly seek the path to co-prosperity between China and Japan. Japan is fortunate, China is fortunate, and mankind is fortunate.

Reading Q&A

Reading Plan (II)

Reply to Mr. He Yongquan and Inform Readers Who Have Obtained Registration Certificates from This Department

From the letters we have received from many readers registered with this department, we see that very few are actually discussing reading plans according to the procedures set by this department. Many readers simply don't pay attention or don't know how to start drafting a plan, yet they hope others will draft it for them. Some readers’ plans, at first glance, are obviously impractical, or are completely based on inexperienced fantasies, or are very carelessly made. However, a plan as seriously and concretely proposed by Mr. He Yongquan based on actual experience is not only a model reference for our readers but also reminds us of the direction in which we should help readers. Therefore, we have published Mr. He's original letter without any changes. Now, we will further discuss it with Mr. He and the general readership.

We completely agree with Mr. He's entire plan. Having a reading plan is like having a plan in life, which can determine a person's success or failure. Since ancient times, there have been many people who, despite being studious and working hard, have not achieved success. There have also been many who, despite seemingly spending little time, have achieved astonishing results. Especially in today's era where scientific methods have become a universal tool, if one is not economical, not only will one achieve nothing, but one will also have no way to start. Therefore, at the beginning of our research, this department wanted to correct readers' scattered attitudes and guide them onto an orderly path of reading life.

The first principle in drafting a [plan] is that it must be based on your actual needs and not just on your own fantasies. Secondly, it should not be empty talk written on paper, but something that can be implemented. Thirdly, the [plan] should consider the whole of what is to be learned, not just a certain part. This [plan] should be part of a whole plan for life, that is, it must have a future. After this part of the plan is completed, it must complete a certain stage, making your understanding more developed.

Therefore, establishing a plan is naturally not an easy task. You have to base it on your experience and level of understanding, and it is also necessary to present it for discussion. We welcome criticism from people with similar experiences.

The above are words of principle. Mr. He's plan has largely achieved this. The reason I am sparing no effort in speaking is because I hope that general readers will read Mr. He's letter based on these principles. At the same time, I also hope that Mr. He will review his own plan to see if it is completely suitable.

The research center proposed by Mr. He is very correct. But unfortunately, we do not know Mr. He's academic qualifications in detail. Based on the points raised by Mr. He and the steps on how to proceed, I dare say that he must have considerable knowledge of economics and the theory and application of materialistic dialectics. Without the former foundation, one cannot recognize the complex relationships of the capitalist economic structure and obtain its essence. The latter is a matter of methodology, and errors in methodology are the same danger. But the biggest difficulty is not the recognition of tools, but how to use them. This is a difficult problem that can trouble many experts. (To be continued)

Chairman Chiang

Approved Special Education Funds for Jiangxi

A Total of 120,000 Yuan Was Allocated from Post-War Reconstruction Funds

The Jiangxi Education Department previously received a telegram from the Provincial Government, relayed from Chairman Chiang, stating that education should be immediately administered in the recovered rural areas of the bandit-affected areas of this province. Therefore, the department drafted an outline of a special education plan for the recovered areas of Jiangxi and submitted it to the Provincial Government Meeting for discussion, resolution, and amendment. The plan budgeted 100,000 yuan to operate 300 people's schools distributed across the recovered counties. The raising of these funds was originally intended to request a subsidy of 120,000 yuan from the Xingying (Chairman's Headquarters) and 60,000 yuan from the Provincial Government to make up the large sum and start the project. As the request for subsidies still had to be submitted by the Provincial Government for review and approval, the implementation date of the Qibu (Plan) had to be slightly delayed. In order to expedite the process, the Education Department first allocated 30,000 yuan from the education fund to operate 53 people's schools distributed across 11 counties, including Yunhua, and is now actively preparing for the People's Education Teacher Training Institute. It is now known that the previous plan has been submitted by the Provincial Government and personally approved by Chairman Chiang, and the requested subsidy has also been approved and allocated from the post-war reconstruction funds (totaling 120,000 yuan). Therefore, there are now 150,000 yuan in special education funds, which can be fully implemented according to the original plan.

The Crisis of Higher Education in China (II) by Luo Jialun

Thirdly, the feeling is that equipment is insufficient. The equipment in Chinese universities is mostly inadequate. To do a good job, one must first sharpen one's tools. Modern science, in particular, requires equipment. Equipment is an important tool for studying knowledge and an important encouragement for studying knowledge. People who run education should save any expenses to engage in equipment. The country should also do its best to subsidize school funding, designating it not for the expansion of administration but for the increase of equipment. China is a poor country. We must never, and should never, use equipment as decoration. Equipment should be aimed at practical research work. People who use equipment should also understand the difficulties of people's livelihoods and cherish and make full use of it. There are also some scholars in the West who have achieved good results in incomplete laboratories and then achieved less than before in magnificent laboratories. However, from the country's standpoint, if you don't want to run a university, if you want to run a university, you should get his equipment right. Also, because there are too many overlapping departments and departments in universities that have not been sorted out, there is too much of the same elementary equipment, and the advanced equipment is too little due to economic dispersion, which is also very regrettable.

Fourthly, there are difficulties in recruiting teachers. This may also be because there are too many universities. The number of universities in China, according to the population ratio, is certainly not too many, but in terms of hiring teachers, there are really not enough scholars in China to allocate because although there are some people who are willing to dedicate their lives to academic research, they are not many. This phenomenon is not only true in China, but also in China, the government and schools are grabbing people, and schools and schools are grabbing people, so there is even more panic about talents. Now, no matter how efficient the government is, the number of students studying abroad and university graduates is indeed unprecedented. Because the school's funding is more difficult, the treatment of professors is not as good as that of government personnel. For example, the treatment of ordinary university professors is mostly no more than three or four hundred yuan, while government officials can be as high as four hundred yuan, and senior officials can be as high as six or seven hundred yuan. Therefore, it is better to work as a technician or section chief in the government than as a professor in a university. If the treatment of university professors cannot be raised to a considerable limit, it may be difficult for everyone to settle down and study knowledge.

According to what I said above, it seems that Chinese universities are difficult to run, but this is not entirely the case. As long as we understand that to settle and have a whole plan and determination to go for it, it is possible to make a radical improvement. There are several reasons why universities are not doing well. Some are from the universities themselves, which they should naturally work hard to improve. Some are from outside the universities, which naturally require the cooperation of all parties. First, basic education should be properly managed, especially middle schools, because it is really difficult to remedy a bad foundation. The government should also strictly examine all public and private middle schools. After the implementation of the unified entrance examination last year, the results of the university entrance examination have been better. This is also a very clear evidence. At the same time, universities should also strictly select new students for admission because university education is not universal education. Even the Soviet Union's education plan only heard that they were striving to create tens of thousands of industrial and technical talents, and did not hear that they were expanding the number of university students by tens of thousands. It can be seen that universities should focus on quality, not quantity. One person with good quality can be worth several people. Now the United States and Japan both feel that there are too many university students. Although the number of university students in China cannot be said to be large, the ratio of university graduates and their unemployment is very large. There are many graduates that society simply cannot accommodate, especially those who graduate from the Faculty of Law. Therefore, I advocate that the first step is to run middle schools strictly, and the second step is to strictly examine and enroll new students in universities. The average cost of each university student to the country each year is about 1,000 yuan or more. These are all the hard-earned money of the people and the burden of the people across the country. Therefore, if the country does not want to train talents, then it is already done. Otherwise, it must ensure that the talents trained are all energetic and useful. Otherwise, students will be unemployed after graduation. Isn't it terrible to be unemployed immediately after graduation? The unrest in politics and society in recent years has all started from this. The current situation of social disorder makes students feel afraid at a glance before graduating. Therefore, they think of various ways to show off in school, and some are willing to be used by others. The future is one of the important reasons. Even the criticism of the head of the department and the professor is not based on their knowledge, but on whether they can find a way out for themselves in the future. Although this is an exception and not entirely the case, it can already make the future of academia pessimistic.

In the past, Zeng Guofan talked about three things to pay attention to when employing people: (1) the way of transferring; (2) the way of cultivating; and (3) the method of examination. Only after the above three points can a true talent be trained. At most, the current schools only do a part of the work of transferring and cultivating. Further cultivation and examination lie in the youth after they take office. In a chaotic society, regardless of the individual's personality and knowledge, only their background, who introduced them, and what power they have are asked. Such a social organization is really extremely dangerous. The use of people is naturally not limited to the government. General society can also accommodate many talents. Therefore, not only must the general national undertakings be developed, but also the general social undertakings must be developed in order to solve the problem of the way out for university graduates. For example, most university graduates in the United States are unwilling to go into politics, because there are many opportunities for development in industry and commerce, and the prospects are better. Why should everyone squeeze into the government to grab food? For example, Ford alone has tens of thousands of people in his company. Every major city in the world has his branch offices and offices, which are more magnificent than embassies and consulates. He is like a lifelong small duke. Why must he be the president? But in China, it is not the case. Various undertakings in China are too undeveloped, while government offices are very developed. Moreover, there are many officials in many government offices, with less work and higher remuneration. Therefore, after being educated, most people are unwilling to go to the countryside and are willing to concentrate in the city. They clearly know that unemployment is very painful, but they are willing to wait for unemployment. They clearly know that the profession is unstable, but it is better to be comfortable for a day. In this situation, not only is politics unstable, but social morality is also declining day by day. If various industrial and commercial enterprises develop together, and their desired treatment is better than that of government offices, then young people will naturally look at the scenery and follow it, their energy will be vented, and their ambition can also be developed. Even those with a desire for leadership can know to take this opportunity to exert it. There is no need for everyone to squeeze into the political arena. You climb on my back, and I climb on your back, and as a result, we all fall into the deep pit and die together. As for the fact that new businesses can absorb most of the talents, it is obvious. For example, the newly opened Hangjiang Railway can prove that Mr. Zeng Yangfu and I said that the Hangjiang Railway employs about 400 university graduates from home and abroad. Please see that a 630-kilometer light rail can already accommodate so many people. Then, there is no need to say more about other larger-scale businesses. In the past one or two years, there has been a notable phenomenon: graduates from the three disciplines of agriculture, engineering, and science in universities have better career prospects, while graduates from the departments of political science, economics, and law feel particularly difficult to find jobs. Therefore, in the past few years, there has also been a change in the trend of young people going to school. More people are applying for the three disciplines of science, agriculture, and engineering than those who are applying for the liberal arts. This phenomenon exists in universities in the north, and it also exists in universities in the south. This is a healthy sign. This is still because the government has recently established farms in the east, farms in the west, built roads in the south, and built roads in the north. The government is always limited. If various social undertakings develop together, the future will be even more promising. The Jiangsu Education Department ordered the distribution to various counties

Method of Compiling Elementary School Local Teaching Materials

The Jiangsu Education Department ordered the education bureaus of various counties, stating that national education is the key to saving the country, and to make the people have a concept of loving the nation, we must first enable them to understand the local area where the nation lives. Elementary school is the foundation of all education. If children can know the excellent customs, rich products, and past role models and historical sites of their native homeland in their daily training, they will be able to arouse the heart of loving the homeland, which will also be able to cultivate the ambition of loving the nation in the future. Therefore, to vigorously promote the promotion of national education, the teaching of each subject in elementary schools must try to adopt local teaching materials as much as possible so that children can fully recognize the value of their local homeland, and then extend to the purpose of loving the nation. The education department previously ordered the organization of a collection committee to collect as much as possible as supplementary teaching materials. This has been ordered to be followed and is on file. Now, in order to improve efficiency and enhance it, nine articles have been specially formulated for the method of compiling elementary school local teaching materials in various counties of Jiangsu. In addition to reporting to the Jiangsu Provincial Government for record, the relevant methods are hereby issued. The head of the bureau should immediately comply with it and, within one week of the arrival of the document, organize the compilation committee and report it to the hall for record. He should also engage in collection in accordance with the provisions of Article 5 of the method and start to draft the main points of the annual teaching materials for each subject and submit them to the hall for review and approval within the time limit. The teaching materials collected in the previous order can be handled together. This matter is related to the key to national education and political affairs. The head of the bureau must deeply understand the hall's long-term attention and strive to comply with it. Do not be negligent or added Han Zhitieqie.

▲Measures for Compiling Local Teaching Materials for Primary Schools in Various Counties of Jiangsu Province

Article 1: The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education has formulated these measures in order to arouse children's awareness of loving their homeland, so as to promote the spirit of the nation and support the people's livelihood. Article 2: The education bureaus of each county, or the county governments of counties that have been abolished, should compile local teaching materials for each subject in elementary school in accordance with the objectives described in the preceding article. Article 3: The content of the local teaching materials for each subject in elementary school compiled by each county should be divided into the following three parts: A. About the past: such as the county's past history, celebrity stories, evolution, historical sites, etc. B. About the present: such as the county's geography, products, customs, habits, economy, places of interest, etc. C. About the future: such as developing the local economy, supporting the people's livelihood, promoting the advantages, correcting the shortcomings, etc. Article 4: Each county should establish a local teaching material compilation committee for elementary schools to compile local teaching materials for elementary schools. The number of committee members should be five to nine. The Education Bureau or the county government that has been abolished will hire people who are familiar with local conditions and who are knowledgeable about elementary school teaching methods to organize it. In counties with provincial-level experimental primary schools or affiliated primary schools, the principal or teachers should be hired as committee members. After the committee is established, the organization charter and the list of committee members should be reported to the hall for record. Article 5: After the local teaching material compilation committee for elementary schools in each county is established, it should collect reference materials in accordance with the principles of each item in Article 3 within one month, and compile the main points of the annual teaching materials for each subject in accordance with the standards of the elementary school curriculum and the important items of each subject operation, and submit them to the hall for review and record. Article 6: After the main points of the teaching materials in the preceding article have been reviewed and filed by the Education Department, the committee should immediately start compiling specific teaching materials, and complete the compilation within three months and submit them to the hall for review, approval, and promulgation as supplementary teaching materials. Article 7: Except for those who have submitted a request to the Education Department for approval due to special circumstances, the Education Bureau or the county government that has been abolished in each county should comply with the compilation within the time limit. If the time limit is exceeded, the county head will be held responsible for the failure to supervise, and should be reprimanded. The head of the bureau or the third section chief of each county that has been abolished will be held responsible for the failure to implement, and should be recorded as a demerit to show punishment. Article 8: The county-run experimental elementary schools in each county should be ordered by the Education Bureau or the county government that has been abolished to bear more compilation responsibilities. If there are any who refuse to remember or delay without doing so, their additional experimental expenses should be deducted as appropriate. Article 9: These measures shall be promulgated and implemented by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education and reported to the Provincial Government for record.

National Christian Universities

Higher Education Conference Opens

▲More than 40 university presidents and expert representatives attended

▲Discussing key issues such as administrative reforms and mergers of departments

All private Christian university schools in the country have specially scheduled to hold a higher education conference from January 19 (yesterday) to 21 in order to seek mutual contact, division of labor, and cooperation to seek full development. The conference was convened by the China Christian Educational Association to discuss important proposals such as the distribution of funds and the reform of academic systems in various schools. The association held an opening ceremony at No. 23 Ming Road, this city, starting at 9 am yesterday. The details are as follows:

University Representatives Attending the Meeting

The representatives attending the meeting included more than 40 presidents and academic deans of the 12 Christian universities in the country, including Bu Fangji, Shen Siliang, and Yili of St. John's University in Shanghai; Fan Zhengkang, Hai Boshi, and Hao Peide of Shanghai Hujiang University; Yang Yongqing, Wen Naisi, and Sun Xiaolou of Soochow University in Suzhou; Stuart Leighton and Liu Tingfang of Yenching University in Beiping; Dei Wein and Meng Enxi of Qilu University in Shandong; Shan Renmei of Fuzhou Union University; Chen Yuguang of Nanjing Jinling University; Wu Yifang, Kang Bende, and Hua Meili of Jinling Women's University; Li Peien and MacMillan of Zhijiang University in Hangzhou; Xiang Yage of Lingnan University in Guangzhou; Huang Pu of Huazhong University in Wuhan; Elsie Reich of South China University; Miao Qiusheng, Beng Lu Aide, Luo Bingsheng, and Ge Deji of the Educational Association; and experts attending the meeting, including Bai Lewu, Bi Lusi, and Wei Lishi.

Important Matters Discussed at the Meeting

The significance of convening this meeting of higher education from various universities is extremely profound, as the educational administration of each university for this academic year will be implemented based on the resolutions passed at this meeting. It is reported that there are over a hundred proposals, covering various aspects such as economic allocation and curriculum reform. According to Shen Shi's reconnaissance, the most important proposals include: (1) The issue of increasing or abolishing departments and faculties in various schools. Because the existing departments and faculties in various schools are often redundant, it is decided to discuss and determine methods for merging and abolishing them based on whether they are needed. Those that are lacking should also be added to achieve completeness. (2) The issue of limiting student enrollment in various schools. In the past, the enrollment of students in various schools often did not conform to the actual situation. Now, it is decided to discuss and decide on this issue, so that the number of students enrolled can be separately stipulated with reference to the actual economic capabilities and equipment conditions of each school, in order to increase educational effectiveness. Other issues concerning teaching policies, changes in the credit system, improvement of school organization, and financial distribution will all be thoroughly discussed. The presidents attending the meeting will also report on the current situation of their respective schools, so as to exchange opinions and refer to each other to achieve the practical effect of division of labor and cooperation.

Shanghai Branch Screens Educational Films

The Ministry of Education's Sports Committee Will Hold a Meeting

▲ Cheng Dengke Has a Proposal

(Beijing News) The Ministry of Education convened the Editorial Committee for the Syllabus of Physical Education Professors in Primary and Secondary Schools this time. The methods for compiling junior high school physical education textbooks have already been decided, and Wu Yunrui and Song Junfu have been recommended to be responsible for their completion, as reported in yesterday's newspaper. The methods for compiling senior high school and primary school textbooks are roughly the same as those listed for junior high school, with no major differences. The compilation of physical education textbooks is limited to the primary and secondary school parts because physical education must start from the root and establish a foundation in primary school before adding appropriate training in middle school to make physical and mental development sound and achieve the goal of revitalizing the nation. Primary and secondary schools are the most common. Once you get to university, you have the ability to choose, and the physical education progress of universities with convenient transportation has almost reached its peak, while the physical education of inland universities is very different. Therefore, it is difficult to set a standard for university physical education textbooks. However, the physical education professors in universities should choose teaching materials that are suitable for the local conditions.

Special Item

The Ministry of Education Sends a Special Envoy to Europe to Study Education

Vocational Education Report

(10)

(C) Advanced Vocational Training

France's advanced vocational schools are the National Conservatory of Arts and Crafts, with a total of six branches located in Aix-en-Provence, Angers, Châlons-sur-Marne, Cluny, Lille, and Paris. The earliest was established in 1776. The National School of Engineering in Strasbourg is also a school of equal standing.

The curriculum of the National Conservatory of Arts and Crafts aims to cultivate engineering personnel and chief engineers. The course lasts for three years, with annual examinations to determine student advancement. Admission requires excellent examination results, with most students coming from national vocational schools or practical schools and secondary schools with higher testing standards. The annual intake of new students is limited to one hundred. The curriculum of the National Conservatory of Arts and Crafts places a strong emphasis on workshop training, with at least five hours of daily workshop practice and only two hours of drafting and engineering subjects, which is its distinctive feature. Graduates have sufficient practical knowledge and are welcomed and employed by the industry.

The National Institute of Arts and Crafts and the Arts and Crafts Normal School also belong to advanced vocational education institutions. The former is a place for researching arts and crafts academics, while the latter is a vocational normal school, a place for training teachers for practical schools.

(3) Private Vocational Schools

The classification of technical personnel at all levels is very detailed and the scope is broad. Therefore, the responsibility for training and education is very heavy. It is difficult for the government to take care of everything, so it has to rely on private forces for assistance. As mentioned earlier, French private vocational schools also have unique features. The government provides subsidies based on their performance to encourage and supervise them. Private vocational schools are also divided into three categories:

(A) Arts Training

Practical industry leaders with far-sighted vision recognize the importance of vocational training for national social economy. Some have established schools within factories to train apprentices, or jointly organized schools by associations and public groups, such as railway bureaus and automobile manufacturers associations, all of which have long been established. Employer associations and labor groups have established technical classes for apprentices in various industries to study. These technical classes are increasing daily, and those with excellent results can also receive government subsidies, with a maximum limit of 50% of recurring expenses, while also being subject to government supervision.

(B) Intermediate Vocational Training

Intermediate vocational training schools or training classes established by private individuals are mostly organized by industrial and commercial associations, similar to apprentice training.

(C) Advanced Vocational Training

Private advanced vocational schools include: (1) The Central School of Arts and Manufactures, which has been established for a century and focuses on training engineering personnel; (2) The Higher School of Commerce, mostly established by local chambers of commerce. (Technical colleges and vocational colleges include private ones and those affiliated with universities). The training of senior engineering personnel is generally divided into two parts. The Central School of Arts and Manufactures and the National Conservatory of Arts and Crafts provide the first part of training, focusing on general engineering knowledge, with a course length of three years. Each vocational college then provides the second part, focusing on specialized knowledge. However, vocational colleges also offer both parts of the curriculum. Famous private vocational schools include the Higher School of Foundry in Paris, the Leather School in Lyon, the Ron Chemical Institute, the Mulo Higher Textile School, the Optical Institute of Paris, the Higher School of Electrical Engineering, and the Higher School of Aeronautics. Those affiliated with universities include the Department of Electrical Engineering, Metallurgy, and Brewing at Nancy University, and the Department of Electrical Engineering and Papermaking at Grenoble University, and the Department of Electrical Engineering and Chemical Engineering at Lille University. Private vocational colleges or schools that have been investigated and confirmed and certified by the Higher Vocational Education Committee as having excellent performance are awarded annual subsidies by the Vocational Education Department of the Ministry of Education to encourage them.

(4) French Agricultural Education

Since the French Revolution, the government has begun planning agricultural education. In 1848, it was stipulated that each province should have one agricultural school, and each district should have one agricultural college and one agricultural normal school. In 1879, it was stipulated that each province and city should appoint agricultural teachers to be responsible for agricultural education in the province and city. In 1912, it was further stipulated that each province should have one agricultural instructor to specialize in the popularization of agricultural knowledge, such as school agricultural courses, agricultural extension classes, and agricultural experimental farms (excluding veterinary and forestry farms), all of which are under their jurisdiction. Each province appoints one or more agricultural lecturers to assist the instructors in compiling lectures and conducting agricultural lectures to impart knowledge to the general public, and their effectiveness is quite significant.

However, the decree of August 1918 stipulated that in addition to agricultural schools, agricultural extension classes, agricultural mobile classes, and winter agricultural schools must also be established specifically to provide rural youth and farm workers with the opportunity to enroll, which will have greater and more far-reaching effects. Therefore, according to the current system, the promotion of agricultural education includes the following levels of schools and training classes: (1) National Institute of Agronomy (Paris); (2) National Agricultural School; (3) Agricultural School; (4) Winter Agricultural School; (5) Agricultural Extension Classes and Mobile Classes.

National Institute of Agronomy (Paris): This institute is the most advanced school of general agricultural education. Graduates of secondary schools must pass the entrance examination to be admitted. Each year, it recruits about 100 new students, while the number of applicants is often more than 500. There are about 40 teachers, all of whom have passed the examination and are appointed by the government. The course lasts for two years. Those who wish to further their studies may enter the River Engineering and Forestry School in Nancy or the Agricultural Training Department established by the Ministry of Agriculture to prepare to be agricultural or horticultural teachers, or to receive training for agricultural and farm workers and managers, or the Department of Physical Chemistry and Natural Sciences to study scientific applications to agriculture. The Cooperative Department provides training for union insurance, lending, and agricultural cooperative managers. The institute has a special department of milk engineering to study milk, oil, and cheese production. After students complete theoretical studies at school, they must go to milk and oil factories across the country for inspection to gain practical experience.

Page 15

Spring and Autumn

Fragmenting the Whole and Integrating the Parts

— Hua Ling

I threw a piece of snow-white silver dollar, weighing exactly seven mace, one fen, and five li, onto the counter of a tobacco shop and exchanged it for six double dimes and ten copper coins. This is fragmenting the whole into parts. Logically, matter is indestructible. If a silver dollar can be fragmented into silver dimes and copper coins, then having six double dimes and ten copper coins should naturally allow them to be integrated into a whole, making a silver dollar. However, in reality, it's not like that. Fragmenting the whole into parts is not a problem, but if you want to integrate the parts into a whole, then you have to dig out three or five more copper coins from your pocket in addition to the six double dimes and ten copper coins. Otherwise, you can forget about integrating the parts into a whole and exchanging them for a silver dollar.

The above example of fragmenting the whole, as long as you are willing to dig into your pocket, subsidize the difference, and suffer a small loss, you can still achieve the point of integrating the parts into a whole, without being completely hopeless. However, we should understand that the seriousness of fragmenting the whole is not just this. Let's take another example. For example, a whole bolt of fabric can be used to make three pieces of clothing. This is also a type of fragmenting the whole. And the parts that are fragmented under this formula of fragmenting the whole will forever be parts, and there will no longer be the possibility of integrating the parts into a whole.

Over the past year or two, the four words "fragmenting the whole into parts" have often been seen in the reports of our Northeast Volunteer Army, and everyone loves to follow it up with the sentence "Wait for an opportunity to integrate the parts into a whole."

The words are indeed spoken lightly and calmly, and are grand and high-sounding, but once a bolt of cloth is cut into two pieces, it can never become a whole bolt again. Even if we take a step back and say that six double dimes and ten copper coins, plus some additional subsidies, can still barely integrate the parts into a whole and become a silver dollar, but in reality, six double dimes and ten copper coins are only worth ninety-eight cents. If a snow-white silver dollar is fragmented into parts and then the parts are integrated back into a whole like this, wouldn't it be finished?

This is indeed a problem full of mystery.

On the Terms of Address Between Two Surnames

— Chen Tao

This article is all about male and female friends. I don't know when I saw an article on titles in this publication. It said that the most common terms of address in the opposite sex are "Mr." and "Ms.", and they gradually change to "Older Brother" and "Younger Sister." (Roughly that's the meaning; I've forgotten the original.) Actually, the terms of address in the opposite sex are really complicated; the first time, the most common term is "Ms.," just like "Mr." However, in addressing a man, you can change to "Brother XX" the second or third time. Going a step further, it's okay to write just one name. There's not much difference in the content of the letter or the friendship. Calling someone "Brother" or using their name doesn't necessarily mean that the two people are in love to a certain degree. However, for women, it still seems a bit impossible, still a bit inconvenient: after calling someone "Ms." the first time, the second time it's not possible to immediately follow with "Older Sister X," "Younger Sister X," or just one name. If you mechanically write like that, people (the other person) must think you're mentally ill, right?

The terms of address are probably more special for Westerners; they or their (sic) first letters to people call people "My dear!" or "Dear..." and refer to themselves as "Your..." I want to try to use that with newly acquainted Chinese friends of the opposite sex, writing something like "My dear..." or "Dear..." and referring to oneself as "Yours..." Then people are definitely going to think you're a horny madman or a pervert.

There seems to be a barrier in the middle, I feel.

"How could there be a barrier..." a friend of mine once argued with me like this: "Chinese people (especially young men and women now) are the best at using terms of address. He or she evolves step by step. The first time you don't necessarily have to use 'Ms.' or 'Mr.' if you already know them. Afterward, the man usually changes it first and at the same time asks the other person to change it too (there are really a lot of tricks: what 'beautiful little bird,' 'lovely rose'; 'great tiger' will also be produced in the same way. [My dearest...][You in the bottom of my heart][The person in my dreams][You who cannot be forgotten] these kinds of nauseating words aren't used much now. Now the most popular thing is just to use the name. What's even more intimate is to use one word. For example, if her name is [Tairy], then you can just write the word [Li]. This is much better than calling her Dear Darling!"

Of course, this also changes with their feelings. Otherwise, you might as well keep calling Ms. all the way, and if you try to change it up and call her some kind of [little bird][rose], she won't pay any attention to you," he added, seemingly having experienced it himself.

Haha... Terms of address have also evolved. It seems like it's a kind of tool for expressing feelings, modern young people! Isn't it?

Year-End Sentiments

— Jian Xin

How can I bear the desolation in my heart? The splendid years are half-worn away. Endless grievances are hard to repay. Limited fame burdens me more and more. I pity Yi for his peaceful simplicity. I am ashamed of my wasted plans for a big catch. Heartbroken, I want to bow in the deep boudoir. The aged Fan Ying sheds tears.

How many cold eyes of people have turned back? The gains and losses are just a pellet. Slander and praise encroach on each other, increasing love and strangeness. Sins and faults cluster together, making it hard to laugh or cry. Since ancient times, entering the world has been worrying about holding a jade. I judge myself to have mistakenly planted a gate at the entrance. I am used to the wind and waves of the lakes and seas. The solitary tumbleweed has long been tied to the carved railing.

Vaguly searching for the past, my heart is lost. The silver pond and the green moon are even more entangled. I occasionally contemplate Zen principles with three thousand verses. I also write one or two poems for the boudoir. The swan's footprints are aimlessly left behind. The clouds and mud ultimately divide people and heaven. I remember that since I put down my pen during the yellow flower season. How many years have passed since I kicked across the autumn river?

A Quiet Observation of the [Exhibition]

In Shanghai, the [big sales] on the market are constant throughout the year. Following the beginning of each solar term, there is a new name to hold a bargain: the newspapers are constantly publishing these kinds of advertisements: all kinds of flags are hung in the streets, flying in the wind. When you go to the streets in your spare time, everything you see and hear is lively, brilliant, and splendid, making you dizzy and fascinated. But what is the meaning of these scenes? People who know a little about the social situation will tell you: this kind of vigorous cheap selling is a symbol of social and economic decline.

The anarchy of all production, this is the characteristic of capitalist society; overproduction, naturally, one must try every means to find a way out. And in this ruthless and acute competition, it is not difficult for us to imagine how many small-capital merchants, because they are squeezed out, encounter tragic fates.

In the past, many literary works have described this situation, such as the new writer Mao Dun's [Lin Family Shop], which is this kind of work. On the screen, this kind of work is really rare. Not long ago, Shanghai publicly screened an American film [Business]; in domestic films, we have only recently seen the only one [Exhibition].

[Exhibition] is a production of the Star Film Company. The story: is roughly very similar to [Lin Family Shop]. It depicts a grocery store in a small town, with an honest small businessman as the protagonist. The whole film unfolds the scene of commercial competition very tensely: the oppression and exploitation of feudal forces, the squeeze of competitors, the threat of the economy, and finally make his store close down, and the protagonist suffers the most tragic fate.

Undoubtedly, this kind of exposure work has its special significance. We can recognize from the screen: what kind of society we are currently in.

The flow of blood can only wipe out strange shame; the rivers and mountains decorated with bloodstains are beautiful, the victory of the blood battle is glorious; those who are willing to shed blood are heroes.

[Taking moving forward as the goal of effort, taking effort as the base point of moving forward:] [Promoting spirit and perseverance, firming will and thought:] are the indispensable conditions for a sound person.

The true color of a village teacher is [thinking about teaching materials when cooking, thinking about moral education when sweeping...]

The final way out for college students is [Lecturer on Practical Love Methods.]

Fourth Battalion Commander of the Northeast

— Zhang Henshui

Episode Twenty-Three

The pain is unbearable, listen attentively to the music

The joy hasn't been exhausted, a hurried message arrives

He explained to himself, "There's no need to blame him. Probably Chinese people are always disgusted with soldiers. They've suffered from soldiers both directly and indirectly, so whenever soldiers are mentioned, everyone feels uncomfortable. Actually, Ji isn't dissatisfied with my son. Even those words he said. Not only shouldn't he scold my son, but he's been helped by my son and should be grateful to him. Why should I make myself angry because of these idle words? What's the point?" He walked into the house in a daze, not even closing the street door, lest he delay important matters. So, with his pipe in his mouth, he slowly walked to the front courtyard, planning to close the gate. At this time, he heard Jiang say, "There are footsteps in the courtyard. Is Little Lin closing the gate? The old master hasn't returned yet. I heard he went to West Mountain with Gan Er Ye." He also heard Guizhi say, "This old gentleman has such interests. Gan Er Ye is a completely new person. How can they talk together?" Jiang said, "In your eyes, you always think Gan Ji is good. Actually, he's nothing special. He's still poor and single. If it weren't for our son-in-law finding him this teaching job, he might still be starving." Guizhi's voice suddenly increased, and she replied, "Why do you slander people like that!" With just this sentence, the room became silent. Old Master Zhao thought, "This is strange. Our bride-to-be is actually helping Gan Ji." He didn't go to the front to close the gate. He quickly ran back to the inner courtyard, sat down on the chair, and slowly puffed on his pipe. The next day, he quietly went into the city and sent a telegram to Ziqiang, telling him to quickly return home and get married. He then invited relatives and friends to step up preparations for the wedding. Five days after the telegram was sent, Zhao Ziqiang carried a load of luggage and walked home. (296)

Shanghai Workers' Cost of Living Index for 1933

The annual Shanghai workers' cost of living index for 1933 has been compiled and officially announced by the Bureau of Social Affairs on time. According to the Bureau's report, the trend of the workers' cost of living index has been downward in recent years. The total index for 1933 was 97, a decrease of 10% compared to 1932 and a decrease of 15% compared to 1931 and a decrease of 17% compared to 1930. Since 1926, except for the index of 93 in 1928 (1926 equals 100), all others have been above 100, with 116 in 1930 being the highest, followed by 113 in 1931. Among the various indices in 1933, the largest drop compared to the previous year was in the clothing category, which fell by 17%; followed by the food category, which fell by 14%; and then the fuel category, which fell by 12%. The miscellaneous category fell only slightly by 3%, while rent showed a slight increase. The table is as follows (1926 equals 100):

Silk and Tea

Silk Waste and By-products Are Slightly Exported

The overall situation is still difficult to be optimistic

Since Japan's abundant silk production has caused an excess in the European and American markets and a sharp drop in prices, it has restricted silk exports in order to raise silk prices. Since the beginning of the year, Japan's silk exports have decreased by 30%. Therefore, factory by-products exported to the United States have been slightly smoother. This month, the American postal ship has 537 packages of yellow and white factory by-products loaded to American-owned New York, Seattle and other ports. India's consumption of our country's silk waste (i.e. silk ends and by-products) has increased sharply, with a monthly demand of 1,000 packages. Therefore, since the beginning of the year, the export of silk waste to the UK has been smoother. In the past half month, 787 packages have been transported to India. However, the overall trend is still difficult to be optimistic. Silk weaving factories in New York are still sluggish in their intake of raw silk, and silk prices are still difficult to stand firm. The opening price of Japanese silk in Lyon is still low, and the price of Chinese silk is still considered too high in telegraphs. Furthermore, the foreign exchange is tight, and the deduction of prices is even smaller. The attitude of European firms in Shanghai is negative. Chinese silk merchants are unwilling to seek sales due to the huge losses in the prices coming from the mesh door. The market is quiet. Yesterday, only the Shanghai Silk Factory purchased 10 packages of yellow factory by-products and 5 packages of yellow soil silk. The price is still sluggish.

Sugar Market

This factory's fine white sugar suddenly rises by 2 dimes

Yesterday, the sugar market was still good due to the upward trend of customs duties and gold prices. The guild's clearing price for No. 24 coarse sand white ordinary goods was 19 yuan and 2 jiao and a half, which was another 5 cents higher than the previous day. The clearing price for transit goods was still 6 yuan and 4 jiao and a half. The price of Dutch red high-quality goods MKGB mark was 15 yuan and 7 jiao, the KO mark was 15 yuan and 6 jiao, and the ordinary goods were 15 yuan and 2 jiao and a half, all of which saw an increase. The price of Taikoo sugar B mark was called at 19 yuan and 7 jiao, but there was no transaction. The price of W mark was 4 jiao and a half, and there were a few transactions. The price of this factory's fine white sugar rose by 2 dimes, and the price of No. 1 Zhenji brand was 18 yuan and 2 jiao, No. 2 was 18 yuan and 3 jiao, No. 3 was 17 yuan and 8 jiao, and No. 4 was 6 jiao. The market trend of Chaoqing turned flat. Yesterday, more than 300 bags were opened.

Metal

Spot tin is extremely scarce

The spot tin market has been very good recently, but the incoming goods are very few, and the market is often in short supply. The spot goods circulating in the city recently are extremely scarce, and the incoming goods are also less, so the standards are rising steadily. For example, the price of Xiaoyan tin is 195 yuan per dan, Dutch tin is 216 yuan, Dou tin is 210 yuan, Xuanzu is 217 yuan, and solder is 62 yuan. It is heard that 2-300 dan of transactions were made. In addition, there were transactions of Jianghua Hengdi Hook light tin and other tin, but the market price was very low and there was no difference.
